RATING: 10
Blood Rage is one of the few area control with action points allowance system & card drafting that I like, because even in death I can still gain glory! It doesn't take long time to finish, the rules are streamlined & easy to understand though there are few cards that's a bit confusing, plus the minis are super awesome! The clans are all cosmetic only with no variable clan power but I still wish for the Ram clan hahaha! The game reminds me of Cosmic Encounter, Game of Thrones, Smallworld & King of Tokyo.

RATING: 5
I'm only rating it this high because I'm aware that one play is not enough to fully judge any game, but man did I not have a good time. Aside from the standard thing of not knowing what any of the other cards were (much less how they fit into the game), you can still only get a heads up on ~2/3rds of all the cards in the draft. Even if you do know what your opponent has, you can easily find yourself strategically blocked off by their combination of cards and positioning, leaving you mostly unable to score in the 3rd age.

Maybe it'd get better with more plays, in which case I'll update this. But holy hell was that a bad first impression.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Blood Rage sure has cool miniatures (or not). Mounting the minis onto a removable bases of varying colours is also a neat solution to denote the owner of the monster. Rules are rather simple and the game can be started quite quickly. 

It is nice that you decide your strategy on the basis of the initial card draft. Thus you can play differently from game to game, sometimes you even have to if you do not get the cards needed for a certain strategy. I also liked that there are two more drafting rounds, when you can make changes to your strategy if needed, or push even further along the path you chose initially.

However, already after the first game everyone in our group felt that we had seen every trick you can pull off during a game, take a few we could not think of. I was not left with an urge to play again to try something different. I take this as a sign of a rather one dimensional game. Yes, the play was fun but it is a shame if you "crack" the code at the first play.

One more thing worth mentioning is the absolutely horrible choice of font. Despite being printed in big and bold the names of the areas are really difficult to read.

The conclusion says that Blood Rage is a nice game but I am afraid it is rather short lived, unless expansions introduce some longevity elements to it.

RATING: 8
Intuitive game with drafting, action-point allowance system and area-control. I really enjoy playing this game even though I am not very good at it. 

I like that there are many different ways to score points in this game. Some tactics even revolve around dying in a region. The skill in the game is to draft a good combination of cards and to use them at the right time. This is not easy as you also have other priorities on the map.

The game works well with both 2, 3 and 4 players. I think I prefer it with 4 though because of the more caotic nature of it. I have not played it with 5, but  I will do as soon as I get my hands on the 5th player expansion. Maybe it is better than 4, or maybe it is too much chaos. Who knows?

I am really looking forward to get more plays out of this game.

RATING: 8
1st play: This game feels related to Chaos in the Old World, which makes sense given the designer.  The drafting is good, and the production values are amazing.  I'm not a big fan of "exclusive" content, especially when it feels like that exclusive content is probably necessary to have a complete game.  I'm not sure if it's a game that will have a ton of replay, depending on how much control over the types of cards you can get.

2nd play: This game was excellent the second time.  Having an idea of what could be played added an additional depth to the game, and the mystics were worthwhile to add.  I'm still not a fan of the exclusive content, but the game was great overall.  Drafting was tight and I saw new paths to victory I had missed the first time through.  Quite excellent.

RATING: 9
I liked this WAY more than I expected to. The draft is delicious and presents some difficult choices, and allows for some planning as well. The area control works well, death has some sting but it never feels mean, and you can turn losses into wins if you plan it well. The blind card play for combat feels very fair as well, since losers get their cards back, and the cards have enough trickeration that you can never be fully sure what the right play is. Leveling up your clan seems to be important above all else, I got +50 pts from level bonuses at game's end, which was nearly half my points. Our quests had people working different areas, would be interesting to see more overlap, although we had PLENTY of conflict. Would be down to play again any time.

also: this is one of the few games I would recommend a broken token for. You aren't getting the expansions in the box without it

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Blood Rage is at heart a streamlining of Lang's earlier Chaos in the Old World with the action transferred to a world of Norse mythology. The competing Viking clans are undifferentiated at the start, but gradually grow more asymmetric through the drafting of upgrades.  The game is less about area control than its forefather; only drafted quest cards reward it.  The focus has switched to winning battles, progressing along three tracks and sending souls to Valhalla.  Some card combos do seem very powerful and there is less variety in the cards than I'd have hoped (a consequence of streamlining?).  All the same, it plays quite smoothly, the tight limits on area occupancy reward forward planning, and the shrinking play area ensures plenty of conflict.

I like the artwork and the minis are very good indeed. The one misstep is the clan of chainmail bikini clad Viking babes.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 10
:arrowE: [u]Synopsis[/u]:
An everyone-is-equal area control game that grows more and more asymmetric as players draft unique cards around the table over three rounds. Glory equals victory points, and glory is won both from winning [i]and[/i] losing battles, completing area control quests, sinking ships, slaying monsters, and pumping up the traits of your battle clan. Don't be fooled, this is not brainless Ameritrash. In fact, it's one of the most finely-honed hybrid games I've ever played.

:arrowE: [u]What I like most[/u]:
I love drafting. But I like drafting the most when it makes sense thematically. 7 Wonders? That doesn't make sense. Sushi Go Party!? That makes a lot of sense. Blood Rage? That makes a lot of sense, too. Players are clans who are effectively bidding for favor from the gods of the Norse pantheon at Ragnarok--these gods need the help of the players to close the end of time, and they dole out their boons to the players on a first-come, first-served basis. Do you want to summon all of the most amazing elemental monsters of the realm? Draft the monster cards from the gods. Do you want to fall on your sword/axe/pike and still gain glory? Draft the Loki cards. Do you want to make your name great in the annals of forgotten history? Draft the Odin cards. Each game I play, it seems as though the progressive asymmetry of the drafting really evokes the desperate theme of the world coming to an end, with only so many able warriors and tacticians left to usher in the apocalypse. In addition to the thematic/mechanical consistency, combat is simple, but also affords an excellent bluffing aspect through card play. This game is FAST, but packs in a ton of tension, player interaction, and satisfying moments within the system.

:arrowE: [u]What I like least[/u]:
Like any asymmetrical game, the fabric of the table can become increasingly fragile if players do not understand no only their own strategy and tactics, but those of their opponents. If the Loki-heavy player is taunting you to pillage so they can send all of their units to die, don't pillage. Quest instead, and deny that player his obvious setup. That said, this weakness for potential fragility is also the greatest strength of the game, as the progressing asymmetry can be incredible if crunched by savvy players.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.3
A game about battling Vikings is something I'm predisposed to be lukewarm about. I don't like direct conflict games, especially of the dice chucking, conquest and fighting over territory variety. Blood Rage is none of those things. It's not even really about Vikings but rather a fantasy Norse mythology world. The game is essentially a euro where you draft cards in order to build combos and point-gaining engines, and then tactically move around pieces on a limited map to gain said points. Fighting is better described as "area majority" and often you don't even want to win. Might be a little too chaotic and random for my liking (and I'm usually fond of a healthy dose of both). The main downside is that if (like me) you don't care about miniatures, the minis make the game far more expensive than I'd normally want to pay for a game like this.

RATING: 9
This has to be one on the funnest games I have ever played.  In my opinion is is a mid-weight game that play in about 90 minutes with 4 players.  It's easy to pickup as the rules are straight forward and intuitive.  Some of the features I like best are:
- Starts symmetrical and uses card drafting to become asymmetrical
- Multiple strategies for winning
- Has tactical as well as longer term strategy play
- Very balanced, good play is rewarded, while mistakes and setbacks don't elliminate you
- Theme is strong and really adds to the mindset and fun
- The minis add to the gameplay

RATING: 7.5
Splendid game for those who don't want to "build civilizations", "save the princess" or "deliver goods to another area", but prefer slaughter and pillaging! If that's you, Blood Rage comes to your aid, with very easy to understand logic but enough variety of cards/choice of action to make the game exciting. Great artwork on the cards and game board, and absolutely gorgeous minis (I've just done 2 clans and some monsters). If you are into painting the figures and are good at it, you'll have a work  of art game. It's not too complex to exasperate a player yet not too simple, it's just right. Not surprised at all that it was made by teh same guy who did my favourite Chaos in the Old World.

There are many paths to victory which is also very good. The haters of it, accuse for its high luck factor and its broken combos. Luck factor is there, yes, but when the 70% of the games out there have dice, you cant really whine about luck in this game. As for the combos, at first it may look like it, but then you realize that there are many different powerful combinations which eventually balance the game.

RATING: 10
First Play 11/29/15

This game is fantastic.  However, I should not that it is easy for someone to min-max in a two player game.  This doesn't make the game bad, it just makes it easy for someone to plow right over the board.

Second Play 11/30/15

This game is still fantastic but the idea of min-maxing is still possible.  The game was a bit more intense this time, but still a min-maxing possibility.  Two player games are much more interesting because there are three destroyed areas at the beginning instead of the one area in the four player game.  Also, we noticed that both the fire giant and the sea serpent are not available in the two player game which took something away.  So I am looking forward to playing this game with four people.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Blood Rage is an (interactive) euro disguised as ameritrash.

The rules are very streamlined: the game lasts three Ages (rounds), and each has five phases. The core of the game are the first two: drafting god's rewards cards, and alternating in taking actions (like play cards, deploy or move miniatures, pillage provinces).

Each player has a clan, and everything is symmetrical at the beginning, but during play every clan takes its own shape in something unique (it is kinda Chaos in the Old World where you build the asymmetry instead of beginning the game with it...).

An interesting game, lighter than it seems, and very enjoyable.

RATING: 8

RATING: 10
Up front, as of writing this, this is my favorite game of all time. So this will just be a list of things I love about the game. Amazing artwork and implementation of one of my favorite themes (vikings). Excellent miniatures, especially the monsters, which by the way, can be yours to control! The miniatures in this game actually made me get into painting miniatures. Drafting for battle cards, upgrades, controllable monsters, and goals for the round all occur at the same time, which leads to people being able to do the strategy they want to do. This game is about getting glory (vikings would be proud) rather than simply winning battles. While winning battles is certainly a good thing, there is plenty of opportunity to get glory by dying in battle, or better yet, in the glorious destruction that is Ragnarok.

Honestly this game appeals to Amerithrash and eurominded gamers alike, and while there is a little too much going on for those who avoid a decent amount of strategy,  most gamers will get this quickly, and will leave with a mixture of satisfaction and longing for that one move back, followed by the desire to get right back into it. I find myself thinking about my plays long afterward and wanting to play again and again.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
I kept hearing Blood Rage was a revamp of Chaos in the Old World and as such I had high expectations from it: sadly, they were all let down the first time I played it. Blood Rage turned out as a dumbed down - and by far not an improved - version of the Warhammer game.

For all practical purposes, it’s an eurogamer’s combat game: that is, a game where players can plan almost everything, go for damage reduction rather than putting everything they have into winning and even arrange a defeat in combat from scratch just because losing a pillage grants them as many points as dominating it, if not more.

As a matter of fact losing battles rather than winning them looks like the best strategy in this game: now, I wonder, how can a combat game reward defeat - and a planned one, for that - more than success?

The simple answer is, it’s a game for those who have no risk appetite: not only is taking risks uneffective here but it also usually backfires as the rules want to prevent you from taking any risk. Unthematically enough, you are not allowed to act rashly but you are required to carefully optimize your every move.
Think, baby, burn your little brain and let the other players wait endlessly for your move. Does it sound any fun to you?

The lack of any dice rolls - that would add some needed randomness in combat - and the annoying card drafting at the beginning of each era as a way to even out the impact of a lucky or unlucky hand simply strengthen this feeling, as they both reward the intricacies woven by the strategically awarer players only: if you’re looking for interaction, theme and epic battles, Blood Rage is not the game for you.

RATING: 9
This is an odd game that I am enthusiastic to play again. It's odd in that the thematic world of the minis, card text and narrative is so coherent but there the connection to the very mathy, combo mechanics seems to be more tenuous than would be expected given what you see when you open the box. Actually playing the game feels a bit like a direct confrontation version of Race for the Galaxy (a game I like a lot)...there is a lot of min/maxing, searching out combos, trying to figure out the chain of when to play certain card combos for maximum point gain. Rarely do I feel like saying, "Roar!" when I put a troll on the board or that I am pillaging when I pillage. As a mathy confrontation game is without question excellent and one I will enjoy playing in the future. The lack of immersion will just keep it from being a ten for me given my penchant for thematic games.

RATING: 6
Despite the hype around Blood Rage, I personally have found it wanting. The production is excellent, and the mechanics are fun. However, the game just feels pointless and unsatisfying at the end. Maybe it's the Ragnarok theme wherein the world ends and everybody dies, but even that kinda misses the mark as most of the board is still intact at the end.
This game is a smorgasbord of gaming elements...card drafting, upgrading, area control, and bluffing, combined with Euro scoring, but it feels like just a taste of each of these.
The game also suffers from a dominant strategy...whoever kills off their own units in the most productive fashion is usually the winner.
I see Blood Rage as kind of a "Hey, check this out!" sort of game. Cool components, silly premise, fun play, but lacks any interesting replayability. Not a keeper.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
12/30/15: First play. I own Midgard but haven't played in 6+ years, and remember little of the details. This definitely feels like that game though, except with the cool minis and way more card actions (including the monsters).

Two of us were new players and the third had played this 4 times before. It seemed like there were a lot of 'fiddly' rules on when things could happen and how cards could be played, and the punishment for being wrong on a rule could be quite severe. In many games being slightly wrong may mean a one or two point swing, but if you did something wrong here it often meant the difference in winning or losing a battle, and that just seemed like a huge impact.

Overall the production values are great, the battling without dice is a strong backbone mechanic for the game, and the card drafting and powers add a nice touch of variety. Definitely looking forward to playing this again with a firmer grasp on the rules. 

05/22/16: Second play, and this game dramatically improved. I had it at a 7 on the first playthrough, but really should have logged it as a 6. Turns out we had a few rules wrong that first play, and knowing better the game going in plus now playing as designed really worked to increase the enjoyment . Felt way more streamlined, less fiddly player interaction, and again, phenomenal production values. Now Jim just has to get his minis painted!

08/19/17:  had best play yet at late-night Gen Con, upping to 7.5. Could go to 8.

RATING: 7
Ameritrash Rating.

Definitely better than the original Midgard which this game is based on.
Simple rules. Can get playing quickly. No convoluted combat. Lasts 1h45m. Doesn't over welcome its stay. 

At heart, the game is about drafting cards - getting the best card combo. It's not really about any conflict. Herein lies the problem. Since the card draft IS the game; the chrome, the board, and the "combat" are really rather extraneous. So aren't there better card drafting games?

As an aside, compared to the other AT flavour of the month, Cthulhu Wars, this is far better.

RATING: 9
sleeved

Once upon a time there was a Kickstarter-campaign to a game called Blood Rage.
The game was really pretty looking with nice miniatures and artwork. But the gameplay wasn't convincing at all. So I let that campaign pass and bought some other games...

...a few months later that game was brought to the stores and people could play and review it.

Man, was I wrong.
This game is a real s***load of fun. I've seen a game of this and instantly fell in love with it.

Components, yeah, we don't have to talk about that.
The only two small complaints are the artwork of the board which somehow looks like it suffers television snow and the small cards. I'm not a big fan of this small format. Especially if you handle them a lot.

The game itself is absolutely awesome with a cool, simple but still very variable gameplay.

I especially like the fact that every strategy can work. Winning battles, loosing battles as well as no fighting at all, every possible strategy can work or fail.

Luckily the game is complete as a retail without the usual CMoN Kickstarter-exclusives (in this game there were just a few).
Another area-control with a twist.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I'm typically not a fan of dudes on a map type games, but that's only part of this game. Players draft cards with new abilities, goals to achieve, battle cards, etc, and then use them to try to gain an edge on their opponents.

As glory can be attained in many ways, even losing in battle, many different strategies can emerge based on what cards you have. The game also encourages action rather than sitting around and turtling, which is great, as turtling is a big reason that dudes on a map games tend to be lame.

Overall, a strong thematic game with some stuff there if you're usually more a fan of cube pushing as I am.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is a preliminary rating, as I haven't played it enough. The components are quite good, of course. My first game was pretty good, but we didn't get to finish. The second game we corrected (hopefully) most of the play mistakes we had made. Due to smart play and good luck on one opponent, I got wiped off the map at the end of the first age, and spent the next two ages far enough behind the leaders to make play painfully frustrating at best. The person who placed second actually was ahead on the board scoring, but the leader tied up by the third age, and had about 40 more bonus points than the second place person. Nobody ended on the same side of the track, scoring-wise. 

I do want to play this more, but I have a feeling it reminds me why amaritrash style games are my least favorite (I still like them). This particular game seems fairly high in the luck department - getting a good combo of cards (and of course taking the right actions to exploit them). Our play time with three player was about 2 hours - some players being fairly AP prone - but of course it felt longer stuck with no shot at a rebound. 

I'll have to see with more plays, but I feel like other ameritrash style games either keep you more involved, or at least eliminate you.

RATING: 7
I'm admittedly not a fan of "dudes on a map" games, but Blood Rage did have a nice mix of Euro and Ameritrash mechanics. To point out the obvious, the minis are awesome and the game looks great on the table. I also enjoyed the card drafting at the beginning of each age to help formulate an overall strategy and introduce some asymmetry between the clans via upgrades. My biggest complaint is that I felt it was hard to really put those strategies into action with the board being so tight in the second half of the game. I felt like my moves were dictated by other people's actions and I just had to react to them instead of focusing on my strategy. But I;m definitely willing to try it again.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Absolutely fantastic.  A tighter yet more wily Chaos in the Old World that runs smoother.  Perhaps the pinnacle of Ameritrash/Euro hybrid.

This would be the perfect game if we had alternate Age decks so the cards/combos didn't get repetitive.  The content discovery aspect of this game is the only thing weighing it down as it feels much quicker to experience and understand than something like Chaos in the Old World.  

Love the game and it's so close to being perfect.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Based on 1 play with 5 players:

Not exactly in love with this, but not bad either. The combat is a bit on the bland side, but the card combos are sufficiently compelling and they're the real meat of the game. The way pillaging works and the Rage resource management work together nicely to give the game some interesting timing considerations. 

I suppose though, if I'm going to go for sub-2 hour Dudes on a Map game it's hard to imagine choosing this over Nexus Ops. Everything here is so transient and opportunistic; my favorite DoaM games are both opportunistic and have some kind of long-term progression. Here, it's really just your three stats which is a little underwhelming.

Totally happy to play this again, but will not be rushing out to get my own copy.

RATING: 8
I'd been curious about this game after hearing about it from a friend. A bit of Chaos in the Old World? Drafting? Sounded good to me!

After one play, I definitely like it. Our group decided it is part Chaos in the Old World and part Kemet. I own both of those games, so I'm not sure I need to own this one, but I'd happily play this anytime. 

Draft cards, spend action points to deploy units to the board or upgrade abilities... gain VPs for generating battles or triggering certain special abilities. It's a Euro game in an Ameritrash skin (much like CitOW), it plays slick, and it was a lot of fun.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I played this more to see what the hype was all about as I really have no interest in this kind of game and I was pleasantly surprised by it. The minis except for maybe the large monsters do nothing for me, but that's not surprising. I'd rather have a hunk of wood with a sticker in my color or even the KS bonus ram heads for everything, than everyone having the same tiny brown pieces because all I look at is the base to figure out who is who. I'll never understand why people throw money at minis, but getting back on point I actually found myself liking this game in spite of my opinion of the lackluster playing pieces. The drafting is neat and the potential card combos are crazy, which really makes the game intriguing to me. My only wish was there was more variability in the cards between rounds as opposed to simply increasing point value for the same card. I guess even that just allows for combos too, but they are not as exciting. Overall the game ran a little long for me, but I can see it being faster with repeated plays and I might actually consider giving it another go, which I would not have thought before playing.

RATING: 7
This is a lovely area control plus special abilities game, a solid design and a great mix of Euro and American style gaming. Unfortunately, it does not compare to its predecessor, CitoW in as much as depth of gameplay and player interaction is concerned. A good game that I'd be happy to play whenever it hits the table.


+ Solid main mechanism and action set, elegant yet functional gameplay
+ Interesting battle mechanism, and due to the battle cards tense and satisfying (although I prefer the dice a la CitoW which give it an epic feeling)
+ Easy to teach
+ Great minis, art and components

= Requires knowledge of the decks to avoid surprises
= Requires people to actively hate draft to stop almost game-breaking combos
= Long with 4 players, but enjoyable so that's fine
= Lacks the brilliant asymmetry of CitoW

- Disliked the (usually unavoidable) "I occupy the whole province and you cannot plunder or invade", too static
- Some upgrade cards, in the German version, had obvious Errata
- The quests seemed repetitive and unimaginative
- Last, one big boo for the Kickstarter exclusives, gameplay is less fun without them, so boo to CMON!

RATING: 8.5

RATING: 9
Fast, furious and fun. Off-the-scale production values with the best board game minis ever produced. But underneath it's actually a great game - it moves fast and there is always something to think about.

The viking theme really comes through with the various incentives to battle - either to defeat your opponents for glory or to lose to your opponents and go to Valhalla for, well, more glory. But even with all the bloody raging around the board it is still a game about strategy and clever point scoring and card play. 

And those minis...did I mention the minis?

RATING: 9
This was like a shot of gaming Viagra. My blood was pumping in places I had nearly forgotten about. I was getting bored by the same theme and mechanics presented in typical euro fare. 

Then this comes along and infuses some really cool minis and a  nordic mythology theme and simply rocked my boat.

RATING: 9
Best rape and pillage simulator out there. Runs very smoothly and has plenty of strategies to explore. Combat is tense.

The upgrade system is excellent. It really helps with replayability. First couple of plays we somehow missed the rule that after playing a warrior/ship upgrade you get to invade with one of those units for free. From experience I can tell you that this is a great design choice.

I understand complaints about the Rage-stealing Loki card, but this isn't meant to be a pure Euro. You need to keep some gas in the tank and resist the urge to run what seems like the optimal lowest-margin Glory-maximizing razor's edge strategy.

Would be nice to have thicker player boards with indentations for the tokens.

A representative of new "small world" like generation of games, fast paced and senseless.
Fun to kill and sacrifice.

RATING: 8
A fairly light area-control "dudes on a map" game. Rules are simple and straightforward. It's a very pleasant and accessible game. All is built upon drafting mechanic, which determines possible strategies. It works very well and encourages creating powerful combos. Nearly all of them seem overpowered at first, but they're all like that, so game balances itself automatically. There are many ways of gaining victory points - even by losing battles. Personally, I don't like camping in one province, taking all the possible spots(because they are limited) and spamming multiple quest cards. Of course it demands some skill to create such a situation but feels just lame and emotionless. The difference between scoring for won battles and fulfilling the quests is sometimes so big that it's not even worth to fight others.

It is said much about the quality of miniatures and it's not without a reason. They are beautiful and full of details. Of course they bump a price, it's obvious. Sure, it could be played with tokens or meeples. But that's the aspect that grabs so much and I see no problem with that. The rest of the components is okay, pretty standard I'd say. Nothing particularly outstanding. 

So why Blood Rage is such a big success? Probably thanks to it's accessiblity, coherent mechanics that all flow together very well, trendy theme(vikings are quite popular recently, aren't they?) and... lots of plastic put into the box. The game brings nothing new, but it plays so smoothly that it deserves a 8 from me.

RATING: 7
Pros:
- Card drafting provides some space for interesting combos and point scoring opportunity.
- Understanding movement tempo and careful timing of unit deployment and placement is key.
- Simple and fast simultaneous card play combat resolution.
- Amazing miniature design.

Cons:
- More of a card drafting game than an area control game. Area majority is important though for scoring.
- Not a lot of room for bluffing despite card play.
- Some floppy spears on miniatures.
- 5th player adds a lot of downtime.

Haven't played enough to make up my mind on this highly successful game. Some games go too long, some are nailbiters, and some are blow outs.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
Rated after 1 play @ 3 players, 1 play @ 5 players

The game looks a lot more complex that it really is. There are only 5 actions you can take each turn, some costing rage from your pool this round. Combat is done using cards and the highest value wins. You can play cards to give you bonuses each round, provide upgrades to your units or add additional units. With 2 new players, it should only take 15-20 minutes to explain almost all the rules. 

The board constantly gets tighter and peaceful coexistence becomes impossible. The beginning of the game felt very solitare to build up your stats and creatures. When the board becomes tight, it's just a mindless slugfest. In one round, I basically ran full steam into the center of the map and managed to pillage it and eliminate a player's entire clan for that round.

It can be fun with 3-4 players willing to not take the game too seriously and just having fun. The fifth player leads to too much downtime. Players who try to optimize everything also tend to drag down the draft or turns and make the game just a painful event.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
2-4

Voorbereiding:

Elke speler kiest een clan en clansheet. Neem de clan’s leider figuur en 8 warrior figuren en plaats ze in de plastic basissen in jouw kleur. Neem je corresponderend schip figuur. Plaats je figuren in je reserve op je clansheet.

Plaats alle monsters naast het bord.

Zet je clan’s glory marker op de 0 van de glory track.

Plaats je clan tokens op de juiste plaats op je clansheet: 6 rage, 3 axes & 4 horns. Plaats je laatste clantoken op de 6e plek van de rage track. 

Plaats de valhalla sheet en de age track sheet naast het speelbord.

Plaats de pillage tokens met de groene rand in de provincie Yggdrasil in het midden van het bord, met de beloning faceup. Schud de andere pillage tokens en plaats ze random faceup op de 8 overblijvende provincies rond Yggdrasil.

Schud de 8 ragnarok tokens en plaats er 1 op elk van de 3 ragnarok plaatsen van de age track, met de tekst faceup.

Plaats het doom token op de provincie die overeenstemt met de provincie die op het ragnarok token van de first age track staat.

Afhankelijk van het aantal spelers, neem x aantal ragnarok tokens en plaats ze met de vernietigde zijde naar boven op de juiste provincies.

5 spelers: geen vernietigde provincies
4 spelers: 1 provincie vernietigd
3 spelers: 2 provincies vernietigd
2 spelers: 3 provincies vernietigd

Een provincie met een ragnarok token is onbestaand. Hierop kunnen geen figuren worden geplaatst.

Sorteer de kaarten op hun rugzijde en maak 3 decks: 1, 2 en 3. 

5 spelers: voeg de 5+ kaarten toe
4 spelers: verwijder geen kaarten
3 spelers: verwijder alle 4+ kaarten
2 spelers: verwijder alle 3+ en 4+ kaarten.

Plaats het saga token op de eerste plek van de first age op de story track.

Geef de startspeler het startspelertoken. Dit token schuift op het einde van elke age door naar de linkse speler.

Elke provincie (gebied) heeft 3 tot 5 dorpen. In elk dorp kan 1 figuur staan. In Yggdrasil kunnen oneindig veel figuren staan.

Er zijn 4 fjorden, telkens tussen twee provincies aan de buitenrand. Elke fjord ondersteunt de 2 provincies die hieraan grenzen. Elk effect dat de provincie beïnvloedt, zal ook de ondersteunende fjord beïnvloeden. In elk fjord kunnen oneindig veel schepen staan.

Speelbeurt:

Het spel duurt 3 ages. Elke age bestaat uit 6 fasen. Verplaats de saga token op de age track. Wanneer de laatste fase van een age is afgelopen, verplaats je de saga token naar de eerste fase van de volgende age tot het spel eindigt aan het einde van de derde age.

1/ God’s gifts:

Geef elke speler 8 kaarten. Elke speler kiest een kaart en geeft de overige kaarten aan de linkse speler. Herhaal dit tot elke speler 6 kaarten heeft. Leg de 2 overgebleven kaarten af.

Spel met 2 spelers: kies steeds 2 kaarten tot elke speler 6 kaarten heeft. Leg de 2 overgebleven kaarten af.

Kaarten van vorige ages worden bewaard op de clansheet.

2/ Acties:

Tijdens je beurt kies je 1 enkele actie. Als je actie rage kost, betaal je de kost door het token op je rage track te verplaatsen. Als je niet voldoende rage hebt om te betalen voor een actie, dan kan je die actie niet meer doen. Als je rage op 0 staat, dan kan je geen enkele actie meer doen (zelfs geen gratis acties).

De actiefase eindigt meteen wanneer alle spelers op 0 rage staan of als alle provincies zijn gepillaged.

A/ Invade:

Kies een figuur uit je reserve en betaal evenveel rage als de STR van de figuur. Plaats de figuur op een leeg dorp in om het even welke buitenprovincie (niet Yggdrasil). Een schip moet in een fjord worden geplaatst.

Invading met je leider kost geen rage!

Als je evenveel figuren op het speelbord hebt staan als het getal op je Horns stat, dan mag je geen figuren meer in het spel brengen.

B/ March:

Betaal 1 rage en kies 1 provincie (geen fjord). Verplaats om het even hoeveel figuren van 1 provincie naar lege dorpen in 1 andere provincie. De provincies hoeven niet aangrenzend te zijn. 

C/ Upgrade:

Je clansheet heeft plaats voor 8 upgrades: 
1 voor elke warrior, leider en schip
2 voor monsters
3 voor je clan

Kies een upgrade kaart uit je hand en betaal evenveel rage als de STR van je kaart. Plaats de kaart op de juiste plek op je clan sheet. Als er geen plaats meer is, leg je de oude kaart af en vervang je ze door de nieuwe kaart.

Troop upgrades: Wanneer je een leider, warrior of schip opwaardeert en je hebt het corresponderende figuur in je reserve, dan mag je deze figuur meteen in het spel brengen (invade) zonder rage te betalen.

Monster upgrades: Wanneer je een monster opwaardeert, neem je het corresponderende figuur en plaats je jouw basiskleur eronder. Daarna mag je het monster figuur meteen in het spel brengen (invade) zonder rage te betalen.

D/ Quest:

Speel een quest kaart facedown op je clan sheet. Dit kost geen rage. Je mag zoveel quests spelen als je wil, zolang je rage niet op 0 staat.

E/ Pillage:

Kies een provincie waar minstens 1 van je figuren instaat (of in een ondersteunende fjord) en die deze rond nog niet succesvol is gepillaged. (pillage token toont de beloning side up). 

Pillage kost geen rage. 

Pillage bestaat uit 3 stappen.

Stap 1: kondig het gevecht aan.

Elke andere speler (van links naar rechts) kan ervoor kiezen om in het gevecht te stappen door 1 of meer van hun figuren van een aangrenzende provincie te verplaatsen naar een leeg dorp van de betreffende provincie. Dit kost geen rage. Schepen kunnen niet verplaatsen. In Yggdrasil kunnen oneindig veel figuren worden geplaatst.

Wanneer er geen vijandelijke figuren in de provincie staan of er zijn geen ondersteunende fjords van andere spelers, dan vindt er geen gevecht plaats. Je neemt de beloning en draait de pillage token naar zijn pillaged zijde. In dit geval verdien je geen glorie door het gevecht te winnen.

Stap 2: speel kaarten.

Elke speler speelt tezelfdertijd 1 kaart uit zijn hand:

Je toont een rode Battle kaart: de +STR bonus wordt toegevoegd aan de totale STR van al je figuren die deelnemen aan het gevecht + alle speciale eigenschappen op de kaart hebben effect.

Je toont een zwarte upgrade of een groene quest kaart: het voegt geen STR toe en het heeft geen effect.

Stap 3: de speler met de meeste STR wint het gevecht.

Bij gelijkspel verliezen alle spelers. 

De winnaar van het gevecht verliest al zijn uitgespeelde kaarten. De verliezer van het gevecht mag al zijn uitgespeelde kaarten terug op handen nemen. 

Alle verliezende spelers moeten al hun figuren in die provincie vernietigen (inclusief de ondersteunende fjords) en verplaatsen naar de Valhalla sheet.

Enkel de speler die de pillage heeft gestart, maakt kans op de beloning van het pillage token (draai het token daarna naar de pillaged zijde). Als de speler die de pillage heeft gestart, verliest, dan blijft de pillage beloning liggen. 

De winnaar van het gevecht wint sowieso glorie gelijk aan hun axes stat, ongeacht of hij de pillage heeft gestart of niet.

3/ De spelers mogen 1 kaart houden voor de volgende age en leggen alle andere handkaarten af. In de derde age moeten alle handkaarten worden afgelegd.

4/ Questfase:

Elke speler draait al zijn quest kaarten om. Als de voorwaarden op je kaart zijn voldaan, dan verdien je glorie (zie questkaart) en mag je 1 van je stats met 1 stap verhogen.

5/ Ragnarok:

Vernietig de verdoemde provincie en vernietig alle figuren in de provincie en de ondersteunende fjords. Deze figuren en fjords gaan naar valhalla. Ontvang het aantal glorie dat op de age track staat voor elke figuur die werd vernietigd. Verplaats het doomtoken naar de volgende verdoemde provincie. 

6/ Bevrijd Valhalla:

Alle figuren van valhalla gaan terug naar de reserves van de betreffende spelers. 

Het einde van een age:

Draai alle pillage tokens terug naar de zijde met de beloning. Geef de startspelertoken door naar de linkse speler. Verplaats het sage token naar de eerste fase van de volgende age.

Het spel eindigt aan het einde van age 3.

Voor elke clan stat dat op de 4e of 5e stap staat, verdien je +10 glorie. Voor elke clan stat dat op de laatste stap staat, verdien je +20 glorie.

De speler met de meeste glorie wint!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

[January 2016 - 9.2]
This game is well worth all the praise it's getting as it hits all the right notes. There's strategy, but the game isn't complicated or difficult to teach. There's minimal downtime as you could be involved in every turn. There's great interaction, but you don't lose the game from losing one or even a couple of battles -- in fact losing battles may be your strategy. And of course, the miniatures and artwork are fantastic.

There's area control, timing, engine building, drafting, battles and bluffing. It reminds me of a mix between Cosmic Encounter and El Grande with hints of Seven Wonders and Hansa Teutonica. 

Drafting is definitely key, and one thing our group has learned is to definitely be aware of what people's strategies are -- especially going into the third round -- and then make sure to take some of the cards they want before they get to them. If you combine a few key cards together from a group, then it can lead to 100+ points in the third round.

There are quite a few over-powerful cards, especially if grouped correctly, so stop opponents via 'hate drafting,' or be sure to build your own powerful group of cards that can match them in points.

That being said, my question with this game is how much legs does it have? There might be the potential to grow tired of the same cards -- as many repeat themselves in rounds 1,2 and 3 (only with different points) -- or does getting to know every card really well just make the game better as you play on?

My guess is that there will many, many expansions that come out to vary the game, although that may start to disrupt some of the balances, especially if one faction (style of play) gets under-represented and another over-represented.

For now, it sits as one of my top-rated games and we'll see how long that lasts.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: N/A
[2016-02-01 -First Impression-]
When my ameritrash loving gaming buddies made me play Blood Rage, I thought: "Oh no, not another Dudes on a Map game!". A few rounds in, I had to revise my first impression. While Blood Rage looks like your typical ameritrash game thanks to all the miniatures and the setting, the gameplay itself surprised both me and my bloodthirsty gaming buddies. In the draft, I made my clan worship Loki and therefore I made a lot of points just losing battles and fulfilling Valhalla quest while the other guys played a more conventional dudes on a map game. My attempt to try something different worked out in the end. While everyone was struggling with the sudden end of a round, which triggers when either all regions have been pillaged or no one has any rage left and reminded me a little bit of Luna, I just made sure I did the two three things I had to do and let my people die in battles afterwards. Surpringsly, this worked and I won by quite a margin.

All in all, in my one and only game of Blood Rage so far, it felt a lot more like a Euro than your typical ameritrash game.

RATING: 8
Blood Rage is a euro-style area control game where the goal is to have the most victory points at the end of three rounds. There are a ton of different ways to get victory points just like a traditional victory point salad euro game.  The mechanics are nicely balanced and elegant, but they do not make much thematic sense. In these regards, Blood Rage is a very well done euro game.  

But Blood Rage also has the direct conflict of an traditional ameritrash game.  It comes with over produced miniatures of amazing quality that make you want to love the game.  And the game play delivers in spades.  While many of the mechanics don't make any logical sense, the theme comes through emotionally by making you feel like you're in the midst of a chaotic battle.  

I love this game.  It's among my favorite of the past 5 years and definitely the best new game I've played in the past 2 years.  It deserves all of the attention it's been getting recently.

RATING: N/A
#: Best 4, 2-4
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Blood rage is an area control game with a twist, in fact there may be several twists. The game is just as much as about drafting, and strategic card play than it is about having the most men on the board and you can even win by having your pieces killed in battle or in Ragnarok .

Overall I like the game, though I feel I prefer Chaos in the Old World (CiTOW) to this one quite a bit.
 
Firstly some Postives:

Short set up time and relatively quick play time.

This game actually plays well with two - which is a massive plus in my book.

Great minis, perhaps the best I have seen in a board game outside of Games workshop, and with no - or minimal - assembly.  There is no need to paint these minis as the plastic already has a little bit of colour (it's like someone fell into the molten plastic) a pinkish tinge and the monsters are a bluey grey colour. They make the models in CiTOW seem like tiddly-winks.
 
Customisable sides, leads to asymmetric powers, and I feel the game would hold up to repeated plays.

Dynamic play, with the board state constantly fluctuating.

The fact that you can have a death orientated strategy via Loki cards is brilliant. Though this information is apparent to other players as upgrades are placed onto your player mat. 

Neutrals:

Board is functional and nice, but not beautiful (that's probably not the right word) I feel its utility reflects criticisms of CiTOW's board for being busily artful, without enough pragmatic considerations, like can you actually fit the miniatures onto the boardspace?
 
The scores aren't as close as I would like so far, and I have some concerns regarding things being 'overpowered', but I'll take it on trust that that is not the case, and it's more a situation of needing familiarity with the cards, which makes your first game(s) a little opaque. Can you choose cards in fitting with any strategy and play well and win irrespective of which strategy you choose? I don't know.
Compared to the board I feel personally that the miniatures are overproduced, they seem to suggest another game which this one is not....

Cons:

What I mean to say is that the game has this steroidal almost mad viking theme, which is lots of fun, but actually it is a thinky and euroesque game more than a 'war' game- I like this fact - but this degree of separation makes the theme seem a bit disconnected.  And the minis increase the price-point a lot. Wooden tokens would have worked just as well and would have mitigated the feeling that I never feel like I am pillaging anything on the board or 'marching', or that my monster - as cool as it is - is actually more than just a number I bring into 'battle' and then manipulate with my  annoyingly small cards. CiTOW also has annoying small cards - it's worth saying that in both games both are small for equally good reason. However I do feel that whatever happens on the board in that game is more thematic - and just a gamer-y if that is what you want. Hence I'd recommend that one over this.


Addendum: I think this is better with 2 than most people give it credit for. Swingy scores with groups of mixed ability/ knowledge of the cards. The wide spectrum of score might be a strength of the game though.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 3
1 demo play, with two rules incorrect (we played that the winner of the battle gets the reward regardless of who initiates the pillage, and without an initial province destroyed) so take it with a grain of salt.

Viewed as a thematic game, it very much limits the range of conflict and drama that can actually occur. Very few pieces in each location, all powers are relatively incremental (with exceptions like the giant that kills everyone at his location.) It's a curious choice for what should be The Ultimate in Theme.

As a strategic game, the card-drafting multiple-path-to-victory doesn't really appeal to me. The connections are fairly obvious (if you get all the points-for-dead-stuff upgrades and the kill-your-own-stuff, you will probably win.) A mix of cards seems a good idea; you don't even have the pleasure of very diverse strategic paths, as would ideally be the case.

I feel it's a hybrid design that takes the worse elements of thematic games (lack of depth, special powers on cards) and strategic (multiple paths to victory, surprisingly low interaction, combo engine pieces).

RATING: 6
It combines action efficiency, engine building, victory point accumulation, and auction-based combat from the Euro sphere with minis, confrontation, and theme from the American sphere. I'd sum it up as an engine building race that incentivizes confrontation. Tension comes from the ambiguous meaning of unit placement, racing for resources, the uncertainty of card play in battle, hidden quests, and the risk of loss in battle. Battles are a three-stage auction with several wrinkles, and actually created some interesting moments. I'd play it again, although I wish the game was half as long.

The production detracts from the enjoyment for me: I'd much rather it cost half as much, have simpler pieces, and employ a theme that wasn't so obviously targeted at men who think that blood and death and monsters and objectified women somehow make a game more immersive.

RATING: 8.38
Oh, this game is so much more than I expected. It turned out it was good choice for [b]Cool Mini or Not[/b] to employ established game designer because [b]Eric Lang[/b] made one great game. And CMON made some amazing miniatures of course. You pick your tribe and everything have the same starting parameters, but then cards are being drafted and your race sheets are being upgraded with unique powers, abilities and allies. And then you pillage Yggdrasil and surrounding lands for blood, glory and Ragnarok. And it plays like that in three rounds. It's fairly quick epic game, leaning slightly, but really slightly toward thematic Euro, which I love.

[b]Update:[/b] Rating modified according to a custom rating system.
[b]Update:[/b] Reduced from 8.60 to 8.38 due some overpowered mechanics allowing dominant strategies favoring repeated losing of battles (I know it's thematic but it's too much of a motivation).

[b]Favorite mechanism:[/b] Drafting your arsenal for the round.

RATING: 10
This is the best game ever!! Simply love it!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
As Chaos in the Old World is one of my favoritest games, I was happy to learn that Lang decided to revisit it on his way to designing Blood Rage.  I was less than thrilled to learn that he was working with CMON, but it worked out pretty well (and admittedly, the minis are cool).

Like CitOW, Blood Rage is an area-control game with a little asymmetry thrown into the mix that is, unlike CitOW, somewhat customizable.  While each faction has a starting base power, you can tailor your faction to your liking so long as you can afford to get the upgrades you want.  This ensures that despite the game starting the same each time you play, there's a good chance that as it goes on, you'll find something different at least through several playthroughs before it gets old.

One of the neat ideas that gets explored here is purposely sacrificing your units to get bonuses.  At first, I thought this might be crippling, but it isn't.  It's pretty easy to get your guys back on the board so it's all the more fun to throw them into certain death just to squeeze some more points out of the deal.

Another thing that distinguishes it from its grandpappy is the card drafting.  Where in CitOW, each player has their own specialized deck to work with, in Blood Rage, everyone shares the card pool and must draft what they want to have for the round.  One of our players coined a nice phrase called, "hate drafting," which turned out to be quite the effective strategy.

On the downside, it seems the three tracks with a potential 60-point swing seems a bit overpowered.  Yes, you can fight against it, but clever play will inevitably end up with someone getting maxed out on the three tracks and if you haven't been paying attention to them, you have no hope of winning.  The other thing I felt lacking was that despite the minis being absolutely beautiful, they drive the price of the game to a ridiculous amount and YMMV, really.

Is BR better than CitOW?  No.  I find that CitOW is a finely-balanced asymmetric game, perhaps the main reason I find it to be one of my favoritesty games.  But that doesn't mean that BR is a slouch - far from it, there is merit to owning both.  While they share similar ideas, they feel distinct from one another, and we even tested that by playing them very closely to one another.

If I may use an analogy, CitOW is a finely-tuned, balanced and powerful GTI where Blood Rage is the little Fiesta ST that is rough around the edges, but still a lot of fun to drive.

RATING: 8
Brilliant.   The game is fairly easy to teach, and the theme and mechanics are mashed together exquisitely. You constantly have to watch what others are doing, weaving your clan onto and around the board in order to find the best scoring opportunities that line up with the cards you drafted.  It's a big sweaty muscle dance.  

I feel like it's a game that you have to play a lot to really start reaping the joy out of it.   The more you and those you play the game with know the cards, the craftier you'll have to get.  It can be kind of tough on new players, because they don't know the cards.  Some of those monster powers can be perceived as jerky if you don't know it's out there.

The one thing I don't like about the game is that winning can feel kind of dirty.  The game revolves around a secret hand of cards that you use to manipulate and mess with everyone else.  Many times, I've felt that the best player in Blood Rage best exploited poor decisions made by the other players, and while that's the case in most games, in Blood Rage it kind of feels mean due to how cards function.  

You can undo a players whole round by throwing down a monster that destroys everything they've built up.  You can lock up a territory (which experienced players probably wouldn't let happen) and exploit it for quest points and stat bonuses, and watch while everyone else decimates each other, and then roll out with a clean up crew - it comes back to everyone needing to have a play or two under their belt (which, admittedly, is not a lot for a decent strategy board game) to level the playing field.  

Unfortunately, I just don't have the mix of players to play this game enough, and for some reason I have a tough time asking someone to play a game called Blood Rage.   My fault.  Not the game.

Despite only giving it an 8, I think it's one of the better, and more engaging games I've played in a long time.

RATING: 7
Blood Rage looks like an ameritrash game... it has 'amazeball miniatures,' a viking theme, and looks like a dudes on a map game. Upon closer inspection, it is really more of Euro game or at least a hybrid (ie Kemet). For example, you're trying to get the most Glory/VP to win the game through an action point system. Unlike most action point games, you won't necessarily use all of your action points before the end of the round and there are ways to upgrade the number of action points you receive at the beginning of the round. I like that all of the factions start symmetrical and differentiate as the game goes on through a wonderful drafting mechanism. It's also great that it's hard to pick on someone... when you start a combat, everyone in the region participates. This game plays quickly, is easy to teach, offers interesting decisions, and looks good as well. Definitely worth checking out, even if the theme/chrome turns you off.

I don't like a sea of grey unpainted miniatures, so I use standees for monsters and meeples for player units:

[img]https://cf.geekdo-images.com/images/pic3005421_lg.jpg[/img]

RATING: 8
Blood Rage addresses essentially every complaint I have with combat heavy games (peaceful observer strategies, swingy dice combat resolution, player elimination, bash the leader, etc), and it does so without opening other holes for players to exploit. Each decision is multifaceted and gives players enough to chew on to stay engaged and focused, but without slowing the game. The constant cage match-style battling leads to some very memorable moments, and the game has an epic air from start to finish. The fluidity of the board-state, and various victory paths facilitate flexible play from round to round, which is quite unique considering the genre, but I still have concerns regarding long-term replayability.

RATING: 6
Faster and cleaner than Chaos in the Old World, but also with a markedly different feel. Here there's much more of an emphasis on timing and ordering of actions (given that combat/pillaging can be called at any time, rather than just at the end of the round). Of course, the draft is a huge component of Blood Rage as well, whereas selecting upgrade cards in CitOW was quite rote. As for drawbacks:  the third (final) round of Blood Rage is one of massive scoring potential, greatly overshadowing the prior two, unlike CitOW in which every round mattered. Also, the necessity of keeping other players in check is much reduced; here you're out for yourself, first and foremost.

RATING: 6.5
Fascinating game and awesome components. The game is quite straight-forward. This seemed to be a game way off my "comfort zone", but it turned out to be good.
What I dislike about the game, is the power of some of the monsters (if a player get a monster card dealt, the other players can be hardly "hurt" by this monster during the round, without knowing it will come into play), and some of the battle cards (at least the one that eliminate the cards played).
Except for those two aspects, I really enjoy it.

EDIT: I had not a very good experience the third time I played it. I now see the disadvantages of some of the battle cards, which could be very destroying and frustrating. A player can build up to a really great battle, putting all efforts in, and then be destroyed by one mean battle card. Next time I play it, I will take the most destroying cards out of the game, and see how that affects the game play and strategies.

RATING: 5
I really wanted to like this one, but its alright... just plain old alright, bit boring, very mediocre, really not worth the hype it has been getting.

The main meat  of the game is the card draft however there are far too few cards to give any variability really as all but 2 cards are in each draft pool. There is also no way to stop a combo of cards once it is in play, this can lead to a win more situation. 

I would much prefer to play seasons for the card draft as there is SO much more variability in the card powers and they ways they interact not only with your board but with what cards everyone else had drafted. This card interaction in blood rage is severely lacking, card-combos usually consist of only two cards.  Age 2 and 3 cards are also significantly better than age 1 cards.

The area control/ board movement aspect feels a little tacked on and the theme really does not show through. In champions of midgard it feels like I am vikings going on epic quests, or defending my village. In blood rage they really could have been anything milling round the board picking fights.  Also thematically why would the frost giants ever be on your side? 

The minis are receiving of a lot of praise but honestly they could have been tokens, and the sculpts are nice, but they are pretty much industry standard,or at least CMON standard, nothing special nothing raising the bar. 

I can see the comparisons between this and chaos in the old world and IMO Chaos is significantly the better game as a lot of the mechanics from chaos have been streamlined to the point of near obsoleteness in Blood rage

Traded with Castles of Burgundy in 2016 for Police precinct & Rococo

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Tried to give this game a chance multiple times but I just can't see why it is so high in the rankings. Every time we play there is a runaway leader problem. 

If you do well in the first round, you will have better stats than the other players and more units left on the map. Which will almost ensure you will also have a good second round and so on.

I also think it is pretty strange that each area has a maximum number of units it can hold. This means you can swarm the map with cheap units and no one will be able to attack you. 

The mission cards are very lack-luster. Almost all of them just require you to control an area of a certain color at the end of the turn. A little variation with different missions would have been nice. It is too easy to see when someone is going for a mission.

The miniatures of course are great and the abilities on the cards are all pretty awesome, but with all the problems mentioned above I just can't enjoy this game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Pretty easy game to learn and very intuitive once you play a round in the game. Card drafting might be the most challenging aspect of the game since you do not know all the cards in the game when you first play and the power creep of cards in the later rounds. There are complaints of overpowered card combinations but in card drafting games, this is always a possibility. Multiple ways of winning the game and the Viking theme and mythology is integrated into the game very well. Very good mix of area control, combat, and card drafting. The different faction in the game all start out the same and differentiate with card drafting and stat gaining from successful pillaging. Very cool miniatures and artwork in the game and highly enjoyed playing the game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Amazing! Deeply strategic and tense. I love how in each game a completely different strategy might call to you: read the signs, go with the flow, and you might end up with a killer combo... or find your plans ruined by someone else. Victory is never guaranteed and you always have to deal with uncertainty. Luck might be on your side or not, but I think it will rarely feel unfair: you will lose mainly to your rivals' maneuvers, not so much to bad luck.

And the theme! Aside from the overly sexualized female warriors of the Serpent Clan, Blood Rage really shines with its enthralling world and ambience. The minis are awesome, with details that surpass FFG quality. Try playing while listening to symphonic or death metal (people would likely believe you if you said Therion's "Secret of the Runes" album was the game's official soundtrack ;)).

RATING: 7
Good Game - But definitely overhyped.

The game is VERY swingy, even for veterans, which makes it quite unpredictable what is going to happen in the mid and end game. A lot of secret information (who got which cards?) along with the design for a lot of confrontation with several players at once lead to a certain lack of control for the players and a randomness of who is eventually going to win - No matter how skilled the players are. 

Also, it does not feel like you fight other players in a wiking battle. Instead, it feels more like you acommodate against a current situation on the board.

Verdict after six plays with four players: Great game, outstanding art and production values - but surely not the best game of 2015.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
An area majority game with decidedly Ameritrashy looks and a Euro character. The heart of the game is the card draft at the beginning of each age which sets the overall direction of what you are going to try to achieve this turn and how you might go about it. Depending on how that turns out losing battles can be just as helpful as winning them, and scoring opportunities abound, with the later rounds dwarfing the early slim pickings. Card knowledge is quite important throughout as many of the cards are almost ridiculously powerful and can easily smash a carefully groomed plan to tiny pieces.

BLOOD RAGE!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Blutrausch. Frakturschrift. Das martialische Cover mit dem Wikinger, der aus blutroten Himmel auf uns zustürmt. Monster aus dem Höllenschlund. Miniaturen. Rasende Wut. Das ganze Auftreten schreit Ameritrash in seinem Urgebrüll. Doch was so barbarisch erscheint ist nur die krachende Verpackung für ein verkapptes Eurogame mit Entwicklungsleisten. Okay, da gibt es das Kampf- und Streitelement mit Walhalla, Ragnarök und nordmythologischer Heldenehre, aber im Grunde ist BLOOD RAGE ein Majority Game klassischer Spielart, angetrieben durch Card Drafting jeweils zu Beginn der drei Spielrunden mit immer kleiner werdender Spielfläche. BLOOD RAGE ist nicht einmal besonders schwer, spätestens in Runde 2 nimmt das Spiel Konturen an. Und als Mehrheitenspiel ist BLOOD RAGE sogar recht fluffig: kein Brainburner wie mancher Euro-Kollege, wenngleich man seine Rundenidee schon planen und durchdenken sollte. Der grösste Verdienst scheint mir, dass es BLOOD RAGE als Formal-Hybrid gelingt die Schubladen von Eurogamer und Ameritrasher gleichermassen zu sprengen. Insofern hat dann doch der Hammer des Thor zugeschlagen.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
The more I get into gaming, the more wary I get of games that get a lot of hype. This one has lived up to its hype for me and my group. Has that perfect weight that appeals to most of my gaming circle. Strategic enough for the heavy gamers, light enough for the casual gamers. In and out in about an hour or so. So much fun!! I tend to be more of a euro gamer myself, but this didnt feel so competitive that it would be off putting. It was all just in good fun. Easy to roll play it up if you wanted to. One of the few games I have picked up lately where I played back to back. I might of been late to the party on this one, but so glad I bit the bullet and picked it up finally. 100% worth it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Finally another game in the "Chaos in the Old World" camp from Eric Lang that does area control, card drafting, and battles in such a nice way.  First off, my favourite part of gameplay is the ability to take a "losing" strategy where the glory of entering Valhalla upon death could be worth big points given certain card combos.  It feels like a very fresh alternative to some other battle games.  The card drafting doesn't so much dictate your turn but gives you options for how you may want to play out your turn and what you want to focus on.  Balancing these cards is important as well as plans may change as you react to other player actions.  CitOW was all about getting a set faction and exploring its possibilities.  Blood Rage allows you to customize your faction through card play, which is excellent.  The different Monsters you can call on are also supremely awesome- not just their miniatures (which are some of the best) but the way they bring up some amped-up power to the game is really cool.  Blood Rage was a little much at times for my poor, puny Euro brain to handle.  There really is no "catch-up" mechanisms.  This means that players must watch each other and prevent each other from pursuing their primary goals too much.  This means some hate-drafting or counter-drafting needs to take place if only to prevent someone else from taking it.  But I don't consider this a fault of the game- it merely sets the tone for a style of game that can definitely be frustrating and painful to those who can't stand to be crushed before their enemies, lamentations, etc. Fans of area control, American-style battle games, and card drafting really should check this one out! It can be punishing and very opaque to new players, but it is a clean, very fluid design. 

2016 - June

RATING: 8
Slightly over-hyped IMO - but a good game.  Really enjoy what the card draft adds to combat.  The theme really works well.  The game has a really good length and a nice weight to gameplay.

I have only ever played with a full table and I am not sure I would want to play with any less.

EDIT: The more I play it the more I like it.  However, my instinct was correct that it suffers at lower play counts.

Also, there is a huge advantage if one player knows the cards better than anyone else or a huge disadvantage if one player simply knows the cards the least.

This would be a really great game for a game group to pick up and then always and only play together as the meta-game would be the most interesting that way.

It's also a completely different game with KS exclusives, much more random.  I think I like it without the exclusives better though...

RATING: 5
Somewhat preliminary rating after 3 plays.

There are a number of moving parts with the area control, special card powers, quests, and drafting. Not sure it's a satisfying game though as there isn't a ton of variety in the cards, and engine-building seems to take a back seat to tactical play. 

As for the production, the minis are definitely nice. Not a fan of the player boards, or some of the artwork. As a card game, you'd have to sleeve the cards to keep them from getting worn quickly. I can't see buying a game this expensive based on the overall game play, but there seems to be a market for this sort of hyped, thematic kickstarter game.

RATING: 8
Is this game a spiritual successor to Chaos in the Old World or Midgard? It has a different feel from both. In CitOW, your race determines your strategy, whereas in BR you have to adapt a bit, depending on what cards come your way. Also, there are no dice. I also like the bluff element with the Loki cards. The minis are highly detailed and the monsters are crazy good. Happy that some of the KS exclusives actually add to the game and are not useless. As for Midgard, well, it was more of a straight-forward area control game with card drafting. It's a fun game, but it certainly lacks the theme that Blood Rage has. I see no reason to own Midgard, but I can see owning BR and CitOW.

RATING: 8.3
A really fun game with a great theme and some amazing figures.  The difficulty and tension ramps up nicely throughout the game and it's possible for players to make late come-backs and win from a long way behind.

The main drawback is the drafting system.  This gives a big advantage to experienced players of the game, who will know good combinations of cards and what to look out for.  Also the cards are unbalanced, with some being much more powerful than others, and each of the 3 ages in the game can be made much easier if you get the right cards.  The last age in particular has one card that helps gain a huge amount of victory points for very little effort and the winner of the last 4 games I've played used this card.

With a bit better balancing of the cards this would be an even higher rated game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
An interesting evolution of "Midgard", keeping the card draft and some of the area majority scoring, but much more focused on combat. I sometimes wish "Blood Rage" was more similar to its predecessor, just with far superior components and artwork, but this is just because I'm more of a Euro gamer. It is more like a Euro-Ameritrash hybrid, but it does well what it intends to do and may please fans of both genres.

The draft that starts each of the three rounds is full of agonizing decisions, as most cards feel overpowered (in a good way) and you don't want to give them to your opponents. Then you play upgrades and deploy troops or monsters that will eventually have to fight to pillage regions. The diceless combat is quick and simple, which is a good thing.

Interestingly, I found a bit of similarity to "Cthulhu Wars" in the way that you spend rage to perform actions and how your clan gains different skills as the game progresses. But "Blood Rage" doesn't have big swings of power and doesn't rely on ganging up on the leader to keep the game balanced. In fact, the dynamics of the game make it very hard to gang up on any one player.

The only real flaw is that the central region, Yggdrasil, may be too important. It increases all your three stats if you successfully pillage it, while other regions increase only one. And since troops that lose a battle are destroyed, it's not uncommon for a player to hold it for the entire game (and most often win).

The miniatures are fantastic, even though I would have preferred the vikings to be in the player colors, instead of identified only by a colored band put around the base. This should have been a solution just for the monsters. Nonetheless, the miniatures really enrich the experience and I probably would rate the game lower if it didn't have them.

RATING: 8
It's a lot of fun, and it's fluid and fast-moving. I have concerns about the cards, though. In principle, yes, drafting should take care of concerns about card balance--but I'm not sure there's much room for hate-drafting in this game. In a game like Fairy Tale, where you will only play 60% of your cards, you could easily hate-draft. But in Blood Rage, you can easily play all of your cards each era, which encourages everyone just maximizing your own strategy's score. If that's true, then I worry that some strategies are vastly superior to others--compare the points for dead dudes vs. ship upgrades, for example.
But it's still very fun and it seems to win friends wherever it goes.
[EDIT] Further evidence seems to be allaying my fears. This sucker appears to have legs.

RATING: 6
This game fell in my estimation after a few plays. Its strategies, while seemingly complex and divergent at first blush, are obvious, its minis underutilized, its board relatively uninteresting, and it has a tendency to feature a runaway leader. In this case, that leader was me. I don't speak from the perspective of sour grapes.

While it is, moment to moment, good fun and theoretically expansive enough, it's ultimately an area control game that has its priorities misaligned and waylaid by cardplay. Those first ten minutes of drafting basically supercede the entire area control aspect. Kemet and Siege of Columbia did a better job of balancing power/engine acquisition and "dudes on a map."

I used to hate drafting. I've since made peace with it and accept it as seasoning (ex: Steampunk Rally), but not as the main course. I'll play this, but there are better options.

RATING: 7
Sure this is a straight euro that disguises as an ameritrash game but its chrome & awesome theme is pretty convincing.
Basically an area control game, with many ways to individualize your struggle for most VP. You can go for brute force, specialisation, numerical superiority, sneaky tactics, or a mix of it.
The game is very tactical because the board is ever changing, so thinking on your feet is more important than any long term strategy.

I wouldn't play this with five again, as it was way too long for my taste. But with three or maybe four this could easily replace games like Kemet or to a certain degree Dogs of War.

Quick, shiny, viking romp.

Update: Yeah 4 is much better than 5! (as usual)

Sadly the kickstarter had many cool things i would kinda miss in the normal version.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
I feel the game is very good, but not the most spectacular game ever in comparison to its hype. The miniatures for the game are everything, which Blood Rage has amazing ones, but the rest of the components leave a little to be desired. Small cards, and decent, but fairly thin player boards, but they get the job done.  The design on the board is functional, but a little drab for my tastes, still it looks good, and definitely better than anything I could design. 

I'm not to keen on CMON's business model. Every big game they publish is kick-started almost always being over-funded. I feel the people who don't fund get skimped on features, such as the inclusion of a 5th player etc. They did this with Xenoshyft as well. But Blood Rage I think doesn't suffer too badly, because almost all of the content can be purchased nowadays outside the KS, unlike Xenoshyft(legendary items and Heroes) and Zombicide Black Plague(literally everything it seems). I personally hate KS exclusives. I understand having a few select things, like metal coins/components, thicker boards or wooden bits instead of cardboard, but taking out mini's or semi-expansion content should solely be a timed exclusive that becomes available later. Meanwhile I need to fork out $100+ just for the Fenrir model and card. 

Look I don't hate CMON by any means. The bring out some amazing  games and have designers who are very talented, but I feel the hype from this game, because of the miniatures, blows itself out of proportion a bit. Not to say I hate the game, because it is in my collection and is great. It's a solid 8-8.5, which is very good in my book, and I think it's a great "next step" game for those that are looking for their first miniatures/area control/dudes on a map fix.

Sadly I can't say the same for the expansions, since they leave a lot to be desired. The "expansions" are basically slight modulations to the core rules, which barely put a dent into the game, as far as new mechanics are concerned. But because of this, it's not a bad idea to include them in someone's first play of it, Blood Rage is due for a nice big expansion that adds more to the game. Maybe new monsters to recruit, a new map, artifacts or sacred weapons players can get that alter their armies, or variable player powers.

RATING: 10
This is great game from Eric Lang that easily ranks in my personal Top 20.  There are nice elements of card drafting, well timed plays, combat, vp scoring, engine building, and area control.  The game is rich in theme and builds throughout with out losing players along the way as long as you play reasonably well.  The game does favor experience.  The only two small issues I have are with the expansion elements the mystics and Loki can both be problems when the players are of disjointed skill levels as the two elements can be more easily manipulated by experienced players to exploit situations that seem to stray from the core game.

RATING: 9
I love this game.  There are multiple routes to getting the VP needed to win, rewarding different strategies; the card drafting means that your strategy isn't scuppered by bad luck, so it's almost entirely skill-based; the fact that rewards escalate through the three ages of the game means that you're never left without a chance of winning, even if you do badly early on.  And and minis are probably the best quality I've seen in a board game.  Brilliant!

Played at a friend's house. Blood Rage - appropriate to the theme - forces a lot of rage, mostly due the result of near-constant combat. There is no true turtling here, and the rather limited number of components makes decisions necessarily precise and meaningful. Cards which can make or break battles are obtained through a drafting system, though the entropy this and the card uses add to the battles are a bit much for my taste in an hour-long game.
