=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Game based on the nordic mythology were different tribes of vikings compete for being the most glorious one. I was very surprised when I first play this game. The owner was explaining the rules and I was thinking "man, these rules are too easy. This game is going to be boring" but, during the game, my interest started to grow as I find myself with several options every turn, and the things to do, were to put the minis, which card to play, what strategy to follow, and just with some very easy rules, the game came alive very smoothly and making a lot of sense. It is true that the mechanics could be applied to very different themes, there is not huge relationship between the vikings and what you do during the game but, however, it is fun to play and there is an adequate strategy and planning that has to be done in order to win.
And then, the great mechanic of the game, clearly, is the Ragnarok. When you first listen about the rule that after each era one location is going to be destroyed because of the Glorious Ragnarok, you think that better get off all my minis from that place, but when you realize that dying under that fireball is, in fact, a great way of earning points, it is when the fun starts.
One of the concerns that I have heard and experienced is that there are some special miniatures that break the balance of the game. I do not think that the differences are that big, but it is a point to be considered.
Positive:
1. Great artwork
2. Great miniatures
3. The Glorious Ragnarok
4. Several strategies are possible
5. Easy to play
6. Drafting mechanic
Negative:
1. Some characters may be too powerful
2. Some expansions should be used
3. Some KS miniatures are no longer available

RATING: 7.5
Arguably I shouldn't be rating this since I only played the first third of a game. But I think I got a decent idea from just that much. I also think it's helped by my rock bottom expectations going in, but I really enjoyed what I played and it seemed like the rest of the game would build on it nicely. When the first round was over I really wanted to keep playing to see the rest of the game.

The card drafting works well, in particular the hands are large enough and the player count is small enough that you'll see hands multiple times. I'm always happy with deterministic combat and it seems like you can do some cool stuff with well timed pillages in terms of moving people around. But I think my favorite thing was the customization and differentiation of the factions and the way that affects the way different players will play. I'd have really liked to see that through to the end to see how the different players developed and what kinds of power combos you could end up with. But already in the first round I was seeing some nice differentiation. I think my first reaction to it was to give it an 8, but between the components and just wanting to hedge a bit I'm going with a 7.5.

In the back of my mind I'm wondering if part of the reason I was as impressed with this game as I was is because it's not a genre I have much experience with. Recently all the new euros I play just feel like more of the same and that hurts their ratings, whereas Blood Rage feels fresh to me, but I can't really say in any qualified manner if it actually is doing anything particularly unique.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Blood Rage is not the usual type of game I enjoy, but it's hard to deny it is good at what it does. It can run a little slow at times, but even in the downtime the tension is off the charts. It also has some unique mechanics - chiefly that losing battles can be part of a valid approach.

It's not all to my liking, though. While there are some events one can plan around, the game is mostly a game of tactics, with only the board state and some upgrades - all of which may or may not be useful based on the cards one sees in the draft. Personally, I enjoy a bit more long-term planning. The game also shrinks the board as advanced tactics and powers appear. This might add tension, but it kills the ability to focus on building an engine - something else I like doing in games.

If this sounds like the kind of game you like, you are gonna love it. But even for those who usually don't enjoy this sort of game, it's worth playing.

RATING: 4
2015-11-24

Initial Rating: 4.0 (November 2015)

I wasn’t expecting much from Cool Mini or Not´s Blood Rage but still the game managed to disappoint me.

The rules are uber easy to grasp, the theme is cool except for the fact that you don´t feel you are a Viking fighting epic battles. Blood Rage is a control area game with some drafting between turns. For me the game fails miserably. 

First I have heard that the game offered “exquisitely” hard decisions in the drafting because all the cards were equally powerful but from my point of view that’s not true. The drafting is obvious in all regards, perhaps at the very beginning you don’t know what to do but after you have a couple of cards you need to pick the cards that complement your previous cards and game situation. It takes seconds to decide this because it is very obvious which card is the best one. I also feel there is a huge unbalance with the cards, for example the monsters can affect the game in a huge way (as the Orc in the first Age) and it is pure luck if you manage to draw one of the powerful ones, there is only one card per monster so it falls to the players to balance the game. To summarize I found the draft to be obvious and the cards to be unbalanced. Lots of uncontrollable luck here.

Second, the area control in Blood Rage fails for me as well because often, the loser of the combat wins almost as many points as the winner, it feels out of sync when a player does this, that is, it feels weird when a control area game allows and rewards a player when they lose control of an area. Besides purposefully losing battles doesn’t fit thematically in any combat game.

Blood Rage also features the (hated by me) “attack the perceived leader” and it lends itself to king-making situations. I heavily dislike both of this characteristics. In our game, it was a foregone conclusion who would win it even before the second age was finished, so it has a rich-gets-richer problem as well.

Blood Rage uses the same core mechanism that Chaos in the Old World (limited number of action points) from the same designer (Eric M. Lang), but the gameplay is a lot easier. When I play Blood Rage I feel I’m wasting my precious gaming time because the decision are too obvious, the game too shallow and its length way too much for what it offers (around 2 hours). I was expecting a heavier experience but the game is much lighter than I had hoped.

As is usual from Cool Mini or Not, the game components are amazing. The miniatures are unbelievable gorgeous and look great on the table. The art is very good as well and that’s the only positive I have to say about the game. Cool Mini or Not´s games usually follow this formula, they are gorgeous, incredible looking games, but sadly, they are also ultimately empty games. I’m clearly not their intended audience. I feel that if the game was regular looking it would not have the success it has today, that is, they put a lot of effort on the outside while the inside is very mediocre.
 
It is a very expensive game.

Bottom line, I know I´m on the very small minority, but I dislike Blood Rage. I feel the ONLY thing the game brings to the table are the marvelous miniatures, everything else fails for me. It has obvious decisions, it is a shallow and light game, its game duration is way too high for such a simple game, it has lots of uncontrollable luck. I would play Chaos in the Old World any day over Blood Rage. Way overrated, I already sold my copy.

Current Rating: 4.0

RATING: 8.25
Fun miniatures war game. Some degree of luck with card availability.  Great component quality. The monsters which special abilities are super fun to handle and deploy and the plastic ring system for sharing monsters in the pool is quite genius. 

Where blood rage shines is that players do not win simply based on succeeding in combat. Instead, players must strategically draft cards and plan their moves to manage their available resources (i.e. rage),to complete quests, and perhaps even lose in battle in order to gain glory points for being in or returning from Valhalla. 

There is luck element which is mostly (but not totally) mitigated by card drafting. For instance a monster upgrade is drawn and kept by the original player the chances of it being passed to the next player is quite low. Similarly, a player may not be able to get a quest card, or a high-numbered battle card, if those cards are retained by the original recipients of the cards.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Six plays in over a three month period, and I I find this game just does it for me. 

Looks? Yeah, obviously. Interaction? In spades - you can't play your own game in isolation, you absolutely have to consider what the others will do as without a doubt it will affect you. Tension? Deciding which cards to pass on can be agonising, let alone which actions to take at which parts of your turn - timing is crucial. Euro-efficiency-mongering - getting the right card combos can be huge, allowing you to really fly. Fights? Oh yes, combat is not scarce or optional (see Scythe), and you had better know which fights to pick and which to avoid. Sneaky? - just check out the Loki cards, the opportunities for turning bad into good are immense.... Man, I love this game.
..............
One play only so far (I'm sure there will be more), fantastic mix of the best bits of Euro-gaming with the tension and interaction of a (light) wargame

RATING: 9
- Very fun, looks great on the table, not too difficult to teach, plays fairly quickly considering the scope, but not so fast that you feel like it definitely needs one more round.
- Haven't played it with 2 players, but I do have the 5 player expansion. Recommend with 4-5 players. 3 can be king-makey, and I expect 2 will suffer from runaway leader.
- I love all the monsters and upgrades, but you have to balance these in the draft. I find this decision process really interesting... I really want this ability, but I know I'll be able to pull off this quest, and that battle card is awesome too... Decisions decisions.
- I also like the timing elements. When to push, when to plunder, etc. You want to do things in a particular order to be as efficient with your rage as possible, however you're often pressured to do things out of sequence to take advantage of an opportunity or prevent someone from throwing a spanner in your works.

Personally, while I appreciate Blood Rage and am definitely willing to play it again, I tend to like games that are more "battles for inches" instead of the "battle for miles" that is Blood Rage.

RATING: 7
Let's start with the miniatures: superb sculpts in the upper echelon of mini quality. Although the female sculpts hardly look ready for a good fight in their skimpy outfits. Sex sells, including on KS. This game is a hybrid ameritrash/euro with the balance scaled towards the 'trash' side. Over three rounds players hate-draft and play a cutthroat take-that area control game where chaos rules and outcomes are hard to predict. Go 'all-in' the first round, lose or get a draw and play a game of catch-up for the remaining time. Card combos are simplistic in nature with very strong take-that effects to make sure you can retaliate out of anger or do some serious leader bashing. Hence the games fitting name: blood rage!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Blood Rage scratches an itch I don't have. A game that achieves its design goals quite well yet I care neither for its parts or sum.

I'm not a fan of card drafting, card combos, special powers, or compounding abilities toward bigger badder moves. I find the game is largely about the draft and moving up the 3 tech tracks with the board as a stage for these things to play out. Early scoring is small and secondary to moving up the tracks and gaining upgrades toward bigger scoring opportunities in round 3. 

I'd suggest drafting/buying cards Dominion style (the game is essentially deck-building/hand mgt from age-to-age) but I doubt it would significantly alter my feelings. As it is, drafting prevents AP and downtime but at the cost of increased luck into a very significant part of the game.

I understand why it's popular: shiny bits, fantasy theme, euro point maximizer underneath; ultimately a familiar song with a new arrangement. It feels like 7 Wonders and Cosmic Encounter but played out on a board with Viking dudes. I bet the Dice Tower crowd is nuts for this. 

A funny aside, despite all the shiny chrome I never really felt the theme. Instead I found it easy to ignore in favor of maximizing points. But hey it's a euro with a lot of chrome. Neither good or bad.

Though not a gateway game in the usual sense, Blood Rage may be a good first step into the world of heavier, dudes-on-a-map strategy games for those who are curious about the genre.

RATING: 7
Much simpler than Chaos in the Old World. CitOW has a much more sophisticated set of interactions among powers and spells and requires players to be much more pro-active about checking one another when they surge for the victory. Blood Rage feels more like a conventional Euro in that players are most interested in building an engine to amass points for victory and strategizing from the draft how best to power their engine. Personally, I prefer CitOW (which has more "story" to it), but Blood Rage is a perfectly adequate substitute for those who want a more teachable and less violent theme.

As an aside, I would recommend letting new players know the possible variety of battle cards and having a reference card for the monsters (so no one gets an unfortunate surprise).

RATING: 10
Probably my favorite game, such that I rate it a 10 even though it is clearly an imperfect one. Balance issues are significant enough that the draft mechanic isn't enough to counter the luck involved with getting the right 1st pick or 2 card combo. This game is more often decided during the draft phase than it should be, but even so it is one of the most fun games you can ever play while losing. Winning feels great. but even getting beat can be hilarious at times. Almost reminds me of Cosmic Encounter or something in that way (which is a crazy but somewhat apt comparison overall).

RATING: 6
From a new player's perspective this is yet another game in the FFG cards-and-creatures mould where action economy and synergies are the be-all and end-all, and the game really rewards you if you get it right, and really stomps you if you don't know what to expect. You may think you're drafting goodies but in reality you've already lost, or maybe someone screws you over with a take-that effect while someone else is running away with the win. I'm kinda indifferent to the theme and minis, but I guess they make it easier to assess parts of the game state. Still waiting for a chance to finish a game of Chaos in the Old World...

RATING: 9.7
What I like about this game is it fixes the snowball effect of conflict games by introducing the Loki deck so the losing players gains things to not fall behind. The winner also loses his combat card so others are more likely to win the following clashes. The drafting is quick but when playing with AP prone people I do two drafts from 4 cards each to make the drafting simpler. As people get stronger you feel like the game will drag on but there are less spaces because of Ragnarok so it evens out. Highly recommend this game!

RATING: 6
2017-03-03 - 7.5 - Finally I managed to play this game. I liked it, however not as much as I could expect from the hype. But still quite a bit. I think that second game can be better, as I know what cards can do. 
It's mostly area control game with fights, which I would like to be a little more exciting. There is not many ways to change number of figures in regions otherwise. 
I like that there are few ways to gain points and you can focus on your individual strategy, but other players still can mess with your plans.
I think I would like to own it but rather from a trade than a shop.

2017-11-04 - 7.5->7 - Is it a big drop? Not really. I just played again and like other games I rated with 7.5 a little better. This one is good too and sometimes it's really nice to jump onto one another. It's fine with 3 but better with 4. I guess the game is a little better as players have some picture what the cards can do and what you can expect.

2017-12-06 - 7->6 - I feel I always rated this game higher than I felt about it, probably because of all the hype and high expectations. It's fine, but I prefer Nexus Ops to have a quick fight with miniatures on a map and Bunny Kingdom to have an awesome drafting experience. This one is OK, but I will get rid of it eventually.

RATING: 7
Fun game with various strategies formed from drafting cards. I like how there's no dice to determine combat results and that you have a good idea what cards other people have from the drafting. Biggest issue is trying to remember what other player's abilities are whilst also managing your own goals.

I suspect the 'death' strategy is probably the easiest as it's harder to stop someone from losing a fight. Tip: don't draft too many expensive cards as you'll exhaust your rage to quick.

Whilst I enjoy it, there's something that stops me from loving it. Can't say it's the luck element in what cards you draft as there are a lot of awesome cards and you will always have good ones to pick. The direct conflict maybe?

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.4
So, is it a hybrid or a pure Euro? It's not easy to answer - it's like a theme-driven Euro that has a strong AT feel. It also seems to have a strong runaway leader problem until players gain more or less the same experience level; after that, multiplayer leader-bashing might help stopping runaway leaders. The game is quite a good fun area majority stuff but it's rather cruel as only clear winners of that area gain anything while the rest are punished hard(removed from the board).
This, combined with the simultaneous card play during area majority 'fights' make it less of the pure euro many claim it to be even though its mechanism elements all can be found in different Euros (mostly about drafting and area majority, a bit even worker placementish). Still, it's quite enjoyable and I guess it's even better when beginner's mistakes aren't made anymore.

RATING: 8
FIRST IMPRESSION:

Really enjoyed my first game with three players. The board becomes squeezed quite quickly and there is no avoiding conflict. The different cards frequently feel overly powerful and it is helpful to know what type of cards are in the deck and have potential to be played. The minis are nicely constructed and detailed as expected. Also think the opportunity to "recruit" two monsters to help quite interesting as some of them look quite intimidating on the board and fits well with the theme. Letting someone win the middle the first two rounds of the game might not be a good idea...

Definitely has some similarities to Chaos of the Old World but this one is a simpler design and one constructs your Viking tribe as the game continues by playing upgrades which will differentiate the different players and their powers a la 7 Wonders style draft at the start of each round. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
june 2016: Last month I decided to treat myself to a big box, epic, Ameritrash style game and I decided on Blood Rage.  I've played Blood Rage three times now and I can state with certaintity: I am absolutely crap at this game. I don't just lose when I play, I get obliterated. The game really doesn't seem to suit me, hence my lower than average score. I've racked my brain as to why the game and I don't click and have come to the following conclusions.

1. Blood Rage is predominantly a card game. Yes, it has a board and yes it has crazy overproduced miniatures, but the game is all in the cards. So much so that if anyone decided to make a cardgame version of Blood Rage, it would need little tweaking. Card games aren't my strongest suit. I am a better strategic player than I am a tactical one. The card drafting at the beginning of each round is highly random. Only extensive knowlegde of the cards and memory of what your opponents choose can slightly mitigate this luck. My knowlegde of the cards isn't good enough, but every time I loose I've lost to players who've played the game for the first time. So card knowlegde can't have been the only factor.

2. Blood Rage is a tableau builder. The player who quickly builds his or her tableau has the edge over other players. And that edge can be very hard to catch up to. In my opinion the game suffers from a runaway leader. Twice have I lost the game because a player with better stats became unbeatable by the other players. End game scores where the winner has twice the points of the other players have been the norm around here.

Some people are under the false impression that Blood Rage is a mixture of a eurogame and an ameritrash game. I really don't agree with that. Blood Rage is an Ameritrash game through and through. The six cards you get each round aren't enough to think of a strategic gameplan. In most eurogames, your strategy is yours to choose. In Blood Rage, more often than not, you're at the mercy of the cards you've been dealt. It is too random and chaotic for a eurogame. And after Eldritch Horror, Imperial Assault and  X-Wing, Blood Rage has started to put me off these American style games. I probably won't get rid of Blood Rage yet. I'd like to see how my thoughts on the game will change after I've played it some more. But Blood Rage has go to be the biggest gaming  disappointment  of 2016 for me.

RATING: 8
+ I like the fast turns (single action).
+ I like how each player customizes their clan throughout the game.  
- The theme is superficial, with card names that don't have much relationship with the effect.  
+ The rules are simple enough. 
$ The game feels smaller than Clockwork Wars, because of the relative lack of flavor, because of the more restricted mechanisms. 
+ Quick battles.
- I can't help thinking that this game (even the base game) has almost too many minis: I prefer games with fewer minis but more game/flavor/richness (e.g. Clockwork Wars). I feel that they add a bit too much fluff to the game.
$ The game feel is essentially that of a series of short combats for quantitative improvements (the 3 tracks), with a constant interaction between players (who compete for the territories), and a progressive customization of each player.
+ The terrain is small enough that many battles happen, with an interesting center that can be joined from everywhere (important for reinforcements), but territories that remain a bit far from each other that positioning is meaningful for battles (too far and you can't reinforce).

Overall: a lean-enough game of many small battles, with limited flavor. Almost a dry euro-like game of battles with some chrome (minis, some background but not much flavor). Well done, though, but not "wide" or flavorful enough for me to be in awe (contrary to Clockwork Wars).

RATING: 8
Initial Impressions: Basically met my expectations but not my hopes, as in it seemed as good as I would imagine from reading the rules, but not as good as the current 8.38 rating + good reviews + finally a good thematic Viking game + factoring in the high cost. As I thought before playing the card drafting doesn't really fit thematically with the game at all. Also I wish there was a little bit more differentiation from each of the smaller unique monsters, some are just stronger versions of others. 

Besides the drafting and the area control the order you perform your actions appear to be pretty important. Also you must choose very carefully which battles you intend to win, as using your high value battle card early can easily screw you over later on if you're not careful. Therefore, this game is more strategic than I thought it would be; the game definitely does not play itself after the drafting phase.

You don't use all the cards each game even for a given player count so there is a little bit variability there.  Also the locations of which bonuses go in which locations and which locations are destroyed create variability too, but we'll see if it's enough as I play this game more. There are multiple ways to score in winning battles, completing quests, purposefully losing some battles with the right set of cards, and getting your units all destroyed by Ragnarok, so at the very least I should be kept busy for a bit in choosing which of those I want to focus more on.

Runaway leader appears to be an issue as if you win battles/complete quests your stats will go up which will allow you to do more stuff later on. 

EDIT: Somehow I've gotten family members who normally can't play anything heavier than Lords or Waterdeep to able have a basic understanding of how this game works. If this proves true for other groups this would be a great boon to this game as being a game I can use has a "next-steps" game without me having to compromise in my game choice. I sometimes wish the combat cards worked similar to Kemet where unit destruction is not directly tied with winning battles, although this would make the strategy to get your units destroyed significantly weaker. 

EDIT 2: There are a lot more cool card combos than I initially anticipated, the core mechanisms of the game have continued to be fairly easy to understand (though there are quite a few less prominent rules that are easy to miss), and I think this game worked very well with 4 players.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
A internesting euro, masquerading as a war game.  The game begins with a card draft.  You then spend rage to take actions on the board or with cards.  Some actions don't require rage like plundering a town.  

The game is incredibly deep.  On the surface, it may seem that aggressiveness will pay in a game called Blood Rage, but actually, it often comes down to timing.  The temporal element of this game is a big factor, and knowing when and where to act is important.  You can spend a lot of cards opposing someone and getting nothing for it.  

The game can be swingy as well.  Odin's throne can really help someone in last place and turn the whole game around for you.  

But on the whole, the game is great.  It may crack my top ten.  Fun family game as well but the kids need to be at least 12 or so to play.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The most over-produced not-really-dudes-on-a-map game (until Rising Sun).  Definitely not a war game despite appearances, as you frequently can earn more points losing battles and sending your figures to Valhalla.  It's a card drafting game with a little bit of area control mixed in.  The cards are what make the game.  You can build your own victory point engine by choosing carefully.  The miniatures are just fun to look at.  If you go in with the right expectations it is a fun game that plays quickly.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
By and far my favorite board game.  Plays great with both my friends as well as my family.  The card drafting phase is a great way for players to select which upgrade/combat/quest cards they want per round as opposed to just a random draw.  

Customizing your clan of vikings is a very neat and rewarding aspect of this game and is governed largely by the card drafting phase.  Players often have to make critical decisions between taking combat cards or upgrade cards.  The addition of the large monsters with added combat bonuses is also a great feature.  

Depending on which cards you choose, you can customize your clan to actually benefit more greatly from purposely loosing battles by using the Loki cards. There are also combat cards that can be played that completely negate the effect of the other players combat cards, steal rage for losing a battle, or make players throw away their combat cards and be forced to select another.  With all of these options available, you never know how the outcome of a battle will play out until it is over.  Many times I've seen small clans beat much larger ones due to proper play of combat and upgrade cards.  Many times in this game, the player who wins the most battles is not the player with the most glory (victory) points at the end of the game.

Overall, this is the best amerithrash style game that I've ever played and I can't recommend it enough.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
There's quite a bit to like about Blood Rage:
-simple, streamlined play
-plays fairly quickly
-card drafting! (something I always find enjoyable)
-clan upgrades (all clans start out the same, but will differ from game to game based on the strategies you pursue & cards you draft)
-limited # of action points per round so you have to be aware of what you want/need to do and plan ahead
-various paths to victory

Cleveland was not a fan so I don't see this staying on my shelf since it's such a large box (and a bit pricey) and is best with 4.  Would likely play Nexus Ops instead (and Cleveland does enjoy that game).  They're not the same mechanically, but close enough game play experience for me.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A fun Dudes-On-The-Map game with lots of playability due to the numerous abilities and monsters to use in the game.  It's surprisingly very easy to teach since all the information is both on the cards and playmat.  In terms of pacing, it plays pretty quickly since you are able to do only ONE action per turn instead of multiple (more board games need to do this).  The game ends shortly after the climax and doesn't overstay its welcome.

However, I don't feel the "need" to own this game.

The first glaring problem with the game is the simple fact that you need to know the decks inside out to play at any competent level.  Otherwise, the game just feels like you are along for the ride with no real direction to follow.  I've seen experienced players take advantage of their neighboring newbies because of newbies didn't realize that passing certain cards to him would just make him powerful.

Which leads to my next issue: The drafting.  It's weak and feels like a mechanic was taped onto the game to "balance" the meta the way auctions were used to "balance" other games.

With all the faults, the game is still very enjoyable but I prefer owning Scythe and the upcoming Rising Sun.  Both games have more open information and first time players can easily understand the game far better than Blood Rage's hidden information within the Age decks.

RATING: 9
I bought this game, and to my delight, my 27 year old girlfriend loves it as well!  We play mostly 2 player and although it's not as fun as 3+, we still find it very fun and balanced as a 2p game.  The minis are SO fun to paint and admire.  Deliciously frustrating for the loser, and glorious for the winner... and both want a rematch ASAP.  Well worth the $75 CND I paid for it.  

Finally, I altered the clan sheets (very good quality card stock).  Using some tin snips and some metal ducting material ($7 at a home reno chain), I cut squares slightly smaller than the clan sheets, and taped them securely to the back.  Now we use magnetic (custom made from simple magnets from a dollar store) markers to track current rage, starting rage, glory/battle, and units on the clan sheets.  No more "accidentally" moving the stock cardboard pieces by bumping the table :D

Strongly recommended overall!

RATING: 6
Rating based on 4 players.

Chaotic but pretty fun. I like the general mechanics of this, but it's *incredibly* swingy, and most of these swings are due to hidden goals (Quest cards). The changing powers of the players was too much to keep track of for me as well. As a result of both of these, it felt like that even though we were interacting and fighting on the board, I had little impact on what others could do because our goals could be entirely different--for a game about warfare, it felt strangely solitaire-ish, and I don't know how I could have done much better. 

There are lots of potential ways to score (it can potentially get a bit point salad-y), but the gameplay is simple, straightforward, and it does feel nice pulling off a good combo and getting a slew of points.  

The minis are very nice, but the difference between the leader and the regular warriors was not big enough.

Certainly not a bad game, and I can see how some of my complaints would lessen with repeated plays, but while I enjoyed my play well enough it's not my cup of tea.

RATING: 9
Good with four and five players (with the 5p expansion). My guess is that it isn't as good with three players, wouldn't try with two.

With newbie players, there's a chance a player might get a unbeatable combo (= Loki) running, when others do not counter draft the combo pieces. I don't mind that.

About 2/3 of the game is in the draft and the rest is in the execution of your chosen plan. Every victory I have seen so far has been achieved by abusing a 2 or 3 card combo (there are plenty of combos available).

I wish they would release a expansion that would completely replace all the three decks. The current expansions are overpriced.

RATING: 6.5
Not a bad game by any stretch, but felt a lot emptier, less thematic, and mechanically dry than I expected. The lavish production doesn't add anything and the gameplay feels like it would suit wooden pieces better than plastic.

I enjoyed the drafting and powerful card combos, and while I appreciate the smooth game flow, play length and simple-enough mechanics, it felt like the design had been streamlined to the point that the 'soul' of the game has been polished right out of it. At no point did I feel like I was raging, pillaging, fighting, or dying for glory, just manipulating the game state to get points.

Comparisons to Chaos in the Old World are accurate on a mechanical level (power points, turn structure etc) but this doesn't have the thematic richness, nor does it involve me as much in the gameplay.

RATING: 6.2
I really want to love this game... I do. The miniatures are fantastic, the theme is great, and the mechanics are straight-forward and easy to learn.

There's a fundamental issue with this game, however, I noticed it during a playthrough and haven't revisited the game since. I found that it's way too easy for one player to become overpowered, early on. I can't pinpoint HOW, exactly, but it might have to do with certain players being able to leave all their pawns on the board in between rounds, while the other players have to use action points to move theirs back on at the start of each round.

I don't know... after one round I got into an argument with my brother about it, and we ended up TALKING about the game/rules longer than we ended up PLAYING the goddamn game! I'd like to revisit it, but there's other stuff that I already KNOW I'll enjoy playing... and at the end of the day that's what makes for a good game.

RATING: 8
Really good game, but not great and not even close to chaos in the old world.  If it were inherently balanced then this would be another story but it relies too much on players having equal knowledge of the game and card combos in order to draft the cards as intended. In fact the game relies on this to balance the card randomness - which is something I don't like with a game with as many mechanisms (fine in 7 wonders). RATING: 8
Good: 
The game has many different mechanics that work well together such as card drafting, unit selection, and area control. 

There are many ways to earn victory points so you don't need to stick with a single strategy type. The mechanics mentioned above will be used to help form your strategy. 

CMON quality minis and components. 

Bad: 
The game doesn't have heavy rules but if you don't understand what you are drafting and formulate strategies off of your draft you will get trampled upon. There were a few newer players that decided the game wasn't fun because of this. 

(related to drafts) As new players to the game it is extremely difficulty trying to overcome the Loki (points for dying) strategy. For the games we have played it feels like the most effective way to win.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Absolutely love this game.  Will not go into too much detail about gameplay, but essentially the game consists of two phases.  In the first you draft cards from the given round's deck, taking a card and then passing the rest to the next player, who in turn is doing the same.  In the next phase you take turns playing your cards, placing your army, and doing battle over the different regions of the board in order to gain rewards and further develop your clan.  Rinse, repeat.  As things progress you get more powerful cards, the game board becomes smaller as regions are destroyed, and more battles inevitably occur.  There are multiple paths to victory, so the most powerful army is not always the winner.  

Pros: 1) Easy to learn, but lots of strategy.  2) Quick gameplay, yet still deep and rewarding.  3) Contents are high quality.  Great sculpts.  4) It's very FUN!  (Isn't that what's most important?).

RATING: 6
The mechanics of Blood Rage are quite interesting and I usually quite enjoy the game when I play it. But after 5 plays (all 4 player games), I find that I tend to leave the table unsatisfied and frustrated. 

I think the main issue I have is that there are too few cards - I've seen them all, and they fall a bit too neatly in a few synergistic groups. I think that adding more cards to the total pool (but keeping the number of cards players keep) would really make the game more interesting to me, as you would not know exactly which cards are in play - and there would be a greater chance of "new" strategies appearing, rather than different people picking from the 3-4 existing paths every game.

Then again, I've found myself often thinking "Huh, maybe it's time to give blood rage another go...?".

RATING: 6
My feeling is just...meh.  This game was totally overhyped.  Maybe I would have enjoyed it more if I hadn't expected so much.  The minis were pretty great looking, but I was unimpressed by most of the other components for the price.  The game and player boards just felt cheap, and I was not that into the artwork.  

Besides that, it wasn't horrible, just not my kind of game.  I had heard that there were a lot of euro-y mechanisms but between the draft and the battle it felt little more than glorified rock-paper-scissors.  This might improve with play and knowledge of the other cards in the game, the varying strategies.  But I just didn't find it that interesting.  I have a love-hate relationship with area control games.  I often don't mind games with some majority bonuses, a very typical euro-type scoring, but games that rely heavily on area control, descendants of El Grande, have never been my favorites.

I would play it again, and I think I could enjoy it a little more, having better expectations going in.  But overall, I just didn't feel the game stood out like I hoped it would, after so many rave reviews.

RATING: 9.9
I backed this one a while ago and it arrived in good order not too soon after it was due (delivered in October with a September projected delivery time); for a KickStarter that’s practically an early delivery. Mrs Fish liked the look of the large packing box (yes, I went all-in for the 5th as well) and decided it would make a dandy Xmas gift for her husbandman. Which it did.

Anyway, over the Xmas break I unboxed the goodies (much to the delight of the Little Fish), read the rules and got pretty excited about the game. From what I could see it was everything that I hoped, add on excellent production values including some superb miniature sculpting and I was keen as keen could be to get it onto the table of honour.

Fortunately, it was pretty easy to find other interested parties and I managed to get in a couple of games at a local games meet-up the first with the base set and the second with both the Blood Rage: Mystics of Midgard and Blood Rage: Gods of Ásgard expansions (discussed below). I also took it along to Cancon and taught it to three new players which was good.

The base game itself is a pretty good game, very engaging and one that has a lot of challenging decisions. Starting the round with card drafting is interesting as it gives a player a chance to ‘read’ the play for the next Age and work out what one’s opponents are up to as well as working out what they need to do. Building a decent ‘engine’ is also rewarded as having complimentary abilities on all your cards is very important. These are skills that will come with experience and should add a lot to the replayability of the game.

The game encourages bold play and there are plenty of ways to score point so that a bad round does not necessarily put a player out of contention. So, in short, a winner a keeper and one game I’d like to play again and again.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.3
A nice accessible game with great components.  The card draft gives each round a unique feel and presumably increases variety from game to game.  The actual turn structure feels both tactical and strategic.  You have an idea of what you want to accomplish for the whole round and each turn presents you with a nice amount of gaming tension as you try to determine actions that will allow you to achieve your overall goal.  It works really, really well.

RATING: 8
From its components I worried that Blood Rage was just going to be another Kemet, (which I despise). Not so!

BR's smart integration of its Norse theme creates a balance in strategy from each card reflecting the personality of God bestowing the Gift. Some give brute force, some are crafty, some favor the underdog. BR's philosophy of honor through death constantly clears sections of the board and relieves the calcified territorial battling that occurs in other area majority games.

The worst thing I can say about BR is I detest its Kickstarter funding. Having discovered the game late there is pretty much no way I'll ever get my hands on the KS Stretch rewards which makes it feel like I'll never get to experience the full game.

Oh, and I think the name is dumb. Blood Rage doesn't conjure to mind a viking game. It's predecessor, Midgard, was a better title.

RATING: 7
A very nice dudes-on-a-map game.  Gets the job done quickly, encourages strategic thinking and tactical flexibility.  Well done, Eric.  So why the 7?  Because without the gewgaws of the admittedly beautiful miniatures, it's an average weight dudes-on-a-map game.  And this leads me to a bigger issue...

This game is being lauded by reviewers who received their $100+ game as a freebie.  I'm glad that these people appreciate this game and are taken in by its design, both as a game and as an object.  But these people are influencers, and these people are conveniently forgetting that for us mortals, us people who don't get free games on demand, we have to pay $100+ for a game that could have been distributed for ($20-60) without the bullshit.

This game is a 10 at $50, and a 7 at $100. I am clearly not CMON's target audience -- it's that simple.

RATING: 7.7
All the production stuff has excellent quality: illustrations, minis, graphic design, cardboard...

It's the best blend between eurogames and tactical ameritrash I've seen lately. It's clearly superior to Chaos In The Old World, as many people claim. The draft mechanism is key, but so is the order of your actions, and adapting to what other players deploy and do on the board... It manages to create tension and maintain it.

On top of that, the gameplay is quite fluid and and it has an good game lenght of around 90 minutes.

Not everything is perfect in Blood Rage, though:
-> Runaway leaders (and players with no hope of catching up) will happen often
-> Some cards seem overpowered :-/
-> Some cards interactions are not covered in the rulebook
-> Not enough cards of each era to reinforce replayability.

Overall, it's a very interesting mix of american and euro games. Able to produce both great and dull games.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
Despite the amazing artwork and fantastic miniatures, make no mistake: This is a Eurogame through and through, not a thematic wargame of any sort, despite appearances. As a matter of fact, the primary mechanics at work here are rather dry card-drafting, area-control, and action-point allocation.

Whether you like these kinds of Eurogames or not, it is hard to appreciate a game that more often than not has wildly differing scores at the disappointingly anticlimactic end; the winning player commonly ends the game with around 100 points more than the person in second place, with players in the middle of the pack rarely ending with scores even within 25 points of each other. Needless to say, almost every player I have shared this game with came away disheartened and frustrated.

Obviously, this game has now been sold.

Euro-AT-hybrid with a clear overweight of the Euro side. With 3 players, too deterministic for me. Way too Euro-ish for me. I want more randomness. RATING: 4
[b]Blood Rage[/b] was sold via auction 10/15/16.

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (6/8 -> 4)[/COLOR]

[i]I had reservations about Blood Rage and they ended up being right. We played a few more times and I just didn't find the game fun. It really is as simple as that, Blood Rage is my least favorite dudes on a map game I've played to date. I normally love drafting in games, but not in Blood Rage. I didn't find the different god cards you draft to be that interesting; most of the synergies were very clear cut and didn't require much thought to execute. Combat resolution was okay, but I much prefer the card based system Kemet employed versus this one. Blood Rage failed to connect all the different mechanisms into a cohesive game play experience. 

I know I am in the minority, but I really don't get the hype surrounding Blood Rage. Is it really the minis? Either way, Blood Rage is a game I'll be avoiding in the future.[/i]

[COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]- Battle resolution is great, you know the strength of each unit but being able to play a card adds uncertainty to the outcome of the battles and adds to the strategy of deciding when to pillage. 
- Relatively quick to set up for this type of game (my biggest gripe with Kemet).
- Not sure how fun the game is with three, I think it may need four to be more competitive, but I'm only two plays in so this may change.
- Mini's are nice, but the warriors all suffer from droopy weapons. Personally I find the mini's from Kemet to be far superior, even the smaller warriors.
- The other components are lackluster, thin player boards, tiny cards and bland board artwork.

I'm not sure where I stand with this game yet, I definitely need and want to play it more. I've played two 3p games with my kids and both have been absolute blow outs. I know part of this is just learning the cards and combos in the game, but I also feel like three players may not be the best player count. I can't even imagine playing with two. I also keep thinking that we are playing things wrong, but I think we got most things nailed down for the second game. It would be nice if the supposed FAQ they are working on would get released. 

As it stands my kids are having fun so it'll continue to get played, but I'm not sure if it'll remain in our collection in the long term. Of course I could also see us really enjoying the game a lot more once we understand the nuances of the game play. Right now if I had to choose I still prefer Kemet, but this game is much easier to set up and teach. I guess time will tell.[/i]

RATING: 8
心得:
賣互動的遊戲
重點在輪抽能不能組合你要的組合技
行動階段則稍微想一下決定執行順序即可
要被圍毆好像也不容易
人多可能比較熱鬧
但是每個城鎮的大小限制又讓人多策略性會降低
算是還不錯的遊戲
模型真的是大加分
規則:
*主圖板跟其餘圖板放置，放一個綠色邊緣的掠奪標記在中央世界樹獎勵面朝上，其餘隨機開著放在其他八個省份，8個滅世標記隨機三個文字面放在時間版圖對應位置上，把末世標記放在該回合的滅世標記指定省分。2/3/4人時隨機拿3/2/1個滅世標記放在其對應省分上，該省分遊戲不使用，根據人數移除對應卡牌再根據牌背洗勻放在時間版圖對應位置上，世界標記紀錄回合
*每人拿一個種族版跟所有模型還有底座，所以模型跟船都裝上該顏色底座或帆，計分標記放0，種族標記放在個人圖板的三個計量軌第一格，跟怒氣值6的位置，隨機起始拿起始標記，每時代結束會左傳
*遊戲進行三輪，每輪有六個階段，利用時間板塊紀錄
1..輪抽階段 之前輪的手牌先放著，然後發這時代的手牌每人8張(第一場遊戲第一輪可不輪抽)，輪抽每次留一張，值到保留6張，剩下的棄掉(2人時一次選兩張)
2.行動階段 怒氣值移到起始格(能力可能讓你增加)，由起始開始輪流動作，需要支付怒氣的就支付，怒氣到0的玩家自動pass，選擇pass的玩家怒氣也自動歸0，在所有人pass或是所有未被毀滅的省分被成功掠奪後，行動階段結束
>侵略  支付等於單位力量的怒氣值放單位到任意外部省分(中間不行)的空村莊上，船要放港灣，放領袖不花怒氣，場上單位數上限等於你圖版的號角數
>移動 花一怒氣移動一個省分(港灣不行)所以村莊的單位到另一個省分的其他空村莊上(包括中間，中間沒單位限制)
>升級 支付升級卡力量值(左上)並放到對應圖板欄位，可蓋掉之前的
*如果是單位(領袖，戰士，船，怪獸)升級，可馬上免費做一次侵略動作
>任務 蓋著出一張任務卡在圖板對應位置，沒上限
>掠奪 選擇一個有你單位(船在港灣也可)位被掠奪的省份進行掠奪
a.從你左手玩家開始，輪流可選擇移動一個相鄰此省分的單位到此省分的空村莊上(不花怒氣，pass玩家也可以做，船不行)，直到滿或每人要進來，如果沒有其他單位跟船在此你直接掠奪成功，直接獲得獎勵將掠奪板塊翻面，但沒有分數
b.出卡牌 每個有單位在此的人暗出一張卡(除非沒牌)，一起打開，只有戰鬥卡增加戰鬥力跟效果，每個人把其單位戰鬥力總和(包括卡牌，沒單位也會算卡牌)
c.結算 戰鬥力最高獲勝，平手都算輸，輸的卡牌都收回手贏的棄掉，輸的人移動所有單位到valhalla圖板，發動掠奪的如果獲勝可拿掠奪獎勵並翻面，如果輸就沒事，然後戰鬥勝利的獲得其個人圖板斧頭值得分數
*一個港灣相鄰兩個省份
3.棄牌階段 棄到剩一張，最後一的時期全棄
4.任務階段 打開任務卡，如果完成條件就拿獎勵，比力量的平手算失敗，會加總相鄰港灣的船
5.諸神黃昏階段 拿此回合對應的滅世標記放到對應省分，毀滅面朝上，所有該省分單位跟相鄰港灣船都移動到VALHALLA圖板，並根據時間圖版的獎勵拿分(2/3/4分在1/2/3時代)，然後移動末世標記到下個要毀滅的省份
6.所以在valhalla版圖的模型回手，所有掠奪標記翻回獎勵面，起始玩家左傳，回合標記下左移
*遊戲在三個時代後結束，加總個人圖板的三個能力額外加分(4/5格+10，最後一格+20)，分數最高獲勝
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
Another Kickstarter game I'm kicking myself for not backing. In my defense, this is typically not My Game; it looks conflict-heavy, dungeon-crawly, plus it had miniatures. But oh my god, this is a really good game! Blood Rage has many elements I love in classic Euros: a great Norse mythology theme, card drafting, multiple "tracks" for resources and victory points as the game's deciding factor for a winner. The game's turns are fast and easy to understand; most of your time in the game will be spent deciding whether you should join battles when another player "pillages" an adjacent territory. Blood Rage is a terrific entryway game for people who want a bit more theme and interactivity than a typical Euro. But the game is also great for veteran players because it has a great foundation of solid mechanics and flawless gameplay. Definitely a recommend for everyone! Now on to painting those miniatures!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A nice re-implementation of Midgard. Doing away with all the placement cards turns the game even further from area majority (the bane of fun), and into a game where you're just slamming guys on to enjoin battle in various areas. Battles are won and lost on the cards you play (gained 7 Wonders style at the start of the round). The really nice thing is you can do well in the game by losing all your battles, as there are oodles of ways to gain points when you lose. It's a matter of building a strategy with your card draw, and flowing with it. I'd happily play it again, but I'm not sure continual conflict games have enough in them to keep pulling me back. Entertaining more than engaging.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: N/A
This game has area control, collapsing territories, card play and upgrades....many good elements. The area control works well and is limited by the zones in a area (once all the zones are filled up, no more units can enter). Territories are destroyed by the Ragnarok in each of the 3 ages; this really tightens up the board and forces players/forces to interact. There are many upgrades, so I can see each game being different. You can upgrade leaders, ships, units, clans, monsters, etc. What you can do on a turn is limited by the amount of Rage you have (which you can upgrade as well). 

One of the most visually stunning parts of the game are the HUGE monster minis. There are 4 included and any player can get them (by spending Rage). 

Overall this is a really fun game. Combat is different, as you only fight if one clan pillages a territory but that's not a bad thing.

RATING: 10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Blood Rage is a game in which players create armies and try to take part in glorious battles before the impending Ragnarok ends the world.  In each of the game's three rounds, players first draft a number of cards that provide special abilities, give them access to new units, grant victory points for certain end-of-round conditions, or help them fight battles.  Players then use their limited resources to deploy their units and fight over the various territories, earning points for the battle and bumps on tracks providing income, increases in the unit cap, and increases in battle rewards.  At the end of each round, a pre-determined region is destroyed by Ragnarok, and units left in that region are killed but earn bonus victory points.  While this seems fairly straightforward, a number of upgrade cards provide "perverse" incentives for losing battles, having your own units killed, etc.  I'm a little concerned that such cards may be overpowered in comparison to normal strategies.  Also, I found it was too easy to "camp" regions, as if a region is full of a single player's units, it's almost impossible to dislodge him.  Despite these misgivings, I found this to be a thoroughly enjoyable game, with a wide variety of interesting strategies and gameplay.

(1 play)

RATING: 9
The buzz about this game will linger in the air for a long time.  Another winner by Eric Lang and certainly the game that made him a household name among board game efficionados.  Blood Rage uses a number of mechanics from card drafting, to area control to card driven combat.  You are vikings fighting for glory before the land erupts in fire and all ends in Valhalla.  But their are many strategies you can employ to gain glory.  Will you be strong in battle?, will you go after quests, or will you submit to your enemy and get glory by dying.  How you play is determined by you and the cards you draft.  Everyone I have played with has LOVED this game.  The artwork is good .. not stellar, but the miniatures are some of the best you will find in any game period!  You have a clan of warriors and a leader but can draft monsters and ships to aid in your quest for glory.  Wow..just wow

RATING: 6

I honestly have not opened up the expansions for this one yet, but I don't see them adding that much variety to this game.  It's a cool looking game, and is a great gateway game for area control noobies.  But there is not enough depth in this game to get me to play it a ton, there's not enough variety of strategy and you are at the mercy of the draft.

RATING: 7
Had some very high expectations of this one, seen the extremely high average rating of 8.2 (03/06/2016), but my one play so far was a sort of a bummer. 
First of all: this is a way overproduced (as the warriors could have been easily replaced with simple cubes like in most majority games) sort of majority game. But my biggest concern is: there seems to a certain number of winning combo-cards and if someone has those, there is simply nothing you can do, apart from waiting until the game is over (which I must admit isn't that long). The only way to solve this problem is to know all those combo's and prevent the creation of such a combo, but that requires a lot of plays of this game off course :s

To end, a sidenote: in the beginning I thought that you could win with a sort of losing-strategy (by the Loki-cards who give you an advantage if you lose) and that would be a cool thing. Then after a full game, I don't think it can compete at all with simply being the strongest one and pillage a province. Simply because pillage improves yours stats, which is a big advantage, as it lets you score even more points by winning a batlle and gives tons of end points at the end of the game as you reached the end of a track.

Edit 12/06/2016: Increased rating after second play as Wim proved you CAN win with a losing strategy. It seems harder, but it's great that you can win by losing :D

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
This is a dudes on the map game, where each player has three stats on their player boards, a limited number of action points, and a pool of units. Players then draft cards which will define their strategies and goals for that round. At the end of the round, a region explodes and gets closed off, making each subsequent round tighter. This game is really fascinating as you explore the ways the different cards and strategies interact. It's also great that combat is only through unit strength plus a single card played, meaning it's diceless. This game satisfies the desire for minis combat and has uprising depth.

:star: Art, Iconography and components functional
:star: Clever or interesting mechanisms
:star: Reasonably low downtime between turns with mildly AP players
:star: Multiple plays stay interesting
:star: Low or mitigatable luck elements
:star::star::star::star::nostar: Raw enjoyment
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Kind of a stripped-down Cyclades, removing many of the finicky mechanics (and, admittedly, some of the complexity and depth).  The miniatures are stunning, the battles are tense, and the rules are fairly simple.  Set up is long, long, long, but the game is satisfying enough to justify the effort.  It is undeniably conflict-based, and that can lead to runaway leaders or players that are left in the dust early in the game, but proper strategy can make losing battles almost as VP-lucrative as aggressively dominating the board.  Plays well with five players (but requires an expansion, which irritates me).  
Probably my favorite CMON game.
Recommended.

RATING: 7
As good as Kemet I guess? But tile "shopping" is replaced by cards drafting at the start of every age to form your main strategy.

Unlike Kemet where battles can be initiated just by invading, BR battles are only initiated if someone pillages a province and neighbouring opponents wish to stop the pillage, provided there's empty spots for them to enter the province or they are already in that province.

Very awesome looking miniatures as well and a clever way to differentiate the leader among the warriors.

RATING: 9
Wow wow wow! Blood Rage was my personal Game of the Year in 2015 and even more than two years later I still play it as much as I can and still enjoy it just as much as I did the first time! The expansions are not a must-have but they add a lot to the replayability and depth of the game.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Wow! What an amazing experience playing this game! Even though I was seriously trounced, I enjoyed every minute of it.  It's one of the most engaging games I've played in a while.  Even when not my turn, I was constantly thinking about my upcoming turn and trying to deduce what the others were trying to accomplish. 

This game combines many different mechanisms in a deeply strategic way. The drafting is crucial, and, as I found, it's just as important to consider what you're passing as to what you recruit. Giving someone, say, two identical quests can really set that person up for a landslide turn for example. Even the deterministic battle was sweat-inducing.  The battles were simple and victory is sweet when you can get it (and want it) and agonizing when you don't.  

My game group loved it as well...even the guy who HATES card-driven mechanisms in games (and who actually trounced us in our first game)!  It's a game I'm eager to get back to the table, and it likely will despite our infrequent game schedule (1/month) and the size of my collection.

The production quality is top-notch. I didn't get the kickstarter version, but honestly, there's so much in this game I don't miss the few extras that came with it.  I appreciate that the retail version has plenty of monsters and alternative sculpts for the warriors.  There's really no excuse for not enjoying the base game.


=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Pros:
1. Fun tactical game with multiple roads to victory
2. Great minis
3. Interesting card combos to explore

Cons:
1. First plays are miserable until you get to know what cards are available.
2. Losing to win is slightly annoying, and slightly over powered.
3. Playing a non-Loki strategy is fun, but extremely high risk as one bad battle can be very difficult to recover from.
4. Suffers from the Family Feud Flaw. The first 2 ages scoring points does not matter. Points all come in the last age.

Summary: The more I played initially the more I liked it. Now the more I play the more I dislike it. This game oddly feels similar to Cosmic Encounters with a bit more strategy. I've already overplayed this game and doubt I will come back to it any time soon.

RATING: 8
Got to play this for the first time 4 player, I have to say it was a blast. The game plays fast and smooth and there really isnt enough time for someone to be a passive player. You have to get in and get your hands dirty FAST. Also a lot of games can have that feeling of not wanting to be "the jerk" but this game doesnt let that happen because everyone is attacking everyone is dying immediately and honestly dying isnt REALLY setting you back and in most cases it scores you points if you play your cards right. 

The main point is that by the time the game was over we were all laughing and having a great time. We sat for about 10 minutes just talking about peoples card synergies and how they were able to score the amount of points they did. 

Doesnt overstay its welcome and honestly leaves you wanting to give it another try. Not sure Id be interested in 5 player but 4 was great.

RATING: 5
This is constantly touted as a great blend of euro and ameritrash gameplay, but I barely recognize the euro mechanics. For me, every second of the game felt like that moment in Yugioh where someone shouts "you've activated my trap card!" Sure, there is little bit of control in drafting the cards at the beginning of each round, but the actual execution of battles is almost entirely unpredictable. You drafted high battle cards? Well, I drafted cards that cancel high battle cards! Bet you didn't see that coming! I won my last game by simply sitting in two zones, filling them up with my warriors, then drafting all of the Quest cards. This is not a good game.

RATING: 2
This is one of my biggest disappointments.  I expected so much because people have touted this game as so amazing.  I very much disliked this game.

First, it seemed to have a huge run away leader problem.  If someone is lucky enough to draft some cards that synchronize well early in the game they can jump to an early lead.  If you weren't able to get many upgrades in the first age AND had your troops destroyed during the first age I don't think you have any chance of coming back.  It's just not fun for that player.

Second, the luck of the draw isn't HUGE, but it's definitely noticeable.  There are decidedly better cards than others for each age and if you didn't happen to draft those cards you are going to have a bad time.

Third, the battling is so over rated.  There are too many battle cards in the game for the amount of battling that will occur.  It's too easy to avoid conflict because it's too easy to stack the odds in your favor.  If you see someone coming into your territory and you can't win, just leave.  This is a bit of a simplification, but I don't want to go into all the details to explain this (it'd take too long).

The miniatures are awesome and the components are pretty great, in general.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Ameritrashy game with some Euro mechanics. Card drafting is the central mechanisms and way to individiualize your clan. Combat is interesting and there is a lot of out-thinking your opponent. Key is to discover combos of different cards/powers and also utilize them to score a lot of points. There is certainly skill involved.

Even though it has no dice and some mechanisms are Euroy, this is a pure Ameritrash game to me. Combat and take-that events are such a major part of the game. But this is also a reason, why I think it is a good but not a great game. 

Miniatures are gorgeous and art (especially on cards) is good. In total I understand why this is the game of the year  for a lot of people.

RATING: 9.5
This game is a revelation.  I am not great at this game.

It combines so many things in so many quality ways.  You have your starting army, you have your starting stats you have a clever mechanism for invading and attacking.  There are no dice.

This game is really well thought out and just a true joy to play, even if Sam Healey stomps you into the ground cause everything that can go wrong in Stage three does.  But it would be a shame for anyone to miss having a chance to play this game.  If you have the opportunity, try it, just be aware, strategies exist to stomp you into oblivion so be aware of them so you can use them or prevent others from doing so.  

Rage on.

RATING: 8
I've only played this once so far, although I expect I'll get to play again before too long. It was a 5-player game, and was really quite a lot of fun. It reminded me more than a bit of Chaos in the Old World (by the same designer), due to the general dynamic of paying to summon units on to the board, upgrading those units to give them special abilities, and having them fight each other, without this fighting being necessarily the whole point of the game. In other ways, of course, it is very different - lacking the asymmetry and the cool alternative routes to victory, but with other elements like the Quests and the 3 different upgrade tracks. Not to mention the crucial card draft at the start of each of the 3 ages, which I suspect between experienced players will constitute the real "meat" of the game. I thought this was an excellent game that I'd love to play again. And the miniatures, particularly the huge ones for the monsters, are very impressive too :)

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
The obvious start to this is that the figures are fantastic. Really detailed and great to look at. The larger monsters have a nice weight to them too. This is, undoubtedly, what will attract a lot of people to playing.

The card drafting aspect is a decent mechanic - it just doesn't work overly well here. Some cards are obviously superb and should always be taken, no choice required. Some are terrible and are easily passed until you're stuck having to take them. The size of these cards is also an issue - why do they have to be so small?

This leads to the most important bit - gameplay. It's an original idea, alright. But it's not really all that good. Area control and fighting, normally a decent concept. The idea of getting points for defeated fighters is unique. But, for a fighting game - it doesn't seem to engross you as actually battling. Throwing men into a hopeless battle, just so you can pick up a few extra VP from their death - doesn't really tie in to the idea the game gives you, of Vikings in glorious combat ending in Valhalla.

The length of the game is also an issue. If you read my reviews, you'll know I'm a big fan of longer games. But when there's not that much happening that I care to track in a game - the longer game just turns into a chore.

So overall, the excitement factor in this game just isn't there for me. It's an OK game that is simple enough to pick up, but would be one I'd have to be talked in to playing again rather than suggesting to anyone to bring it.

RATING: 6
Blood Rage is meh for me. There's nothing special about the drafting of the outlandishly tiny cards. All the "hype" comes from the miniatures, and I am not one to get very excited about miniatures. There is a problem with catching up to the leader; a bad first age means you are almost certainly going to lose the game. Playing against experienced players is a nightmare, and you'll almost definitely lose then too. While I'm criticizing, I also think spending "rage" as a resource is a little tacky.

Aside from this, the art is pretty good, and the combat system is interesting. I'm a fan of the board slowly shrinking turn after turn, squeezing the players together and forcing more interaction. The center space fights also add a lot of tension. These are really neat mechanics that are enough to make me want to play at least a few more times. Not a game I own or want to own, but I'll play it with the right people from time to time.

RATING: N/A
reddit 2015 recommendation
"Blood Rage deserves a spot on this list, for a couple of reasons:
It nails asymmetric gameplay, allowing each viking clan to create their own identity through the course of the three eras.
It plays very fast, oftentimes having an era end before you expect it, meaning you can't mess around
It encourages aggression to the highest degree, very much like Kemet, meaning there's no time to sit back and watch or build up - it's time to fight right out of the gate
The Battle cards are incredible, and allowing up to all 4 (5 with expansion) players to participate in a single battle blows most other similar games (Kemet, as good as it is) away when they only allow 1v1 at a time.
The shrinking amount of space to fight only reinforces all of the drive towards aggression."

RATING: 9
:thumbsup: Great graphic design. Clear but thematic spaces on the game board. Your player board doubles as a player aid for the different turn actions.
:thumbsup: Many equally valid paths to victory, all leaving room to sabotage other players' well laid plans, or to bluff about your own intentions.
:thumbsup: It looks way more complicated than it is. Rules are easy to explain.

----

:thumbsdown: A sceptic could say this is an overproduced game.
:thumbsdown: Experienced players often have the upper hand over new players due to their knowledge of the types of cards that are in the decks. The first time(s) you play, you're mostly familiarizing yourself with the different ways to win rather than really having a shot at winning against more experienced. I've seen this discourage some new players.

RATING: 10

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
THIS is my number one game of GenCon 2015. After one play under my belt, it was an instant hit.  After half a dozen plays, it is one of my favorite games.

I bought this on a whim on the first day because I knew it was going to sell out quickly.  I'd heard good reviews form several podcasters who all had wildly varying tastes so I knew there had to be something to the game that would appeal to me.   

Honestly, it is one of the best games I've ever played.  There is no fluff in this game.  Everything is essential.   One of the comments I've read said there is "chrome just for the sake of chrome" in this game.  I can't get on board with that statement. The minis are over the top gorgeous, of course, but everything else was so streamlined, from the uncluttered board to the functional, intuitive player mats.  It's not one of those huge FFG games with 1000 components.  There aren't dozens of different damage markers and status icons, etc...Everything has been stripped to the bare essentials in this game short of reducing the Minis to wooden cubes.  

There is so much to like here, but I'll focus on my favotirite thing:  Card drafting.  The card drafting is amazingly agonizing.  Not because you cann't find cards you want, but because every card is incredible.  You want them all.  And you know everyone else wants them all, and you definitely don't want to pass them anything juicy but you are going to!  The choice is between a fantastic card and several other fantastic cards.  Drafting is also easy for new players.  Each card is associated with a particular Norse God - just pick one or two names to focus on, draft them, and you'll have a great engine all ready to go!  But the great thing is that you don't really have to get locked into one particular strategy - you can change your strategy from round to round just by drafting a different set of cards.

This also plays surprisingly well with two, even though I miss seeing more variety in cards each round.  

Instantly one of my favorite games of all time.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
I really really enjoy this game.  It might very well be the best game in my collection right now.  Why does it deserve such high praise?

1.  Relatively simple ruleset.  It is very easy to learn this game and teach others how to play.  You could absolutely teach a non-gamer Blood Rage, as long as they've had *some* gaming experience (e.g., Risk) in their past.

2.  Great pacing.  The draft is engaging and simultaneous.  Individual player actions are quickly resolved.  Battles do not take up an inordinate amount of time, but are very tense and meaningful.  You can finish a game in under 2 hours if your players don't lag.

3.  Strategic.  There are multiple pathways to victory, as in Questing, Conquering, and Loki.  You can mix and match, and even switch your focus mid-game and still win.  You need to be careful about drafting, and what you pass to certain players.  But it's also not hard to come up with a strategy and just pursue it to see what happens.

4.  Components.  Amazing.  I wish the board wasn't quite so heavy-metal, but other than that, wow.  This contributes enormously to engagement.

Downsides?
1.  Losing hurts.  You can find yourself out of the running pretty quickly, if you have a poor first age.  I did this one game by following a poorly structured Loki strategy that backfired, and the rest of the game was somewhat tedious for me since I knew I was out of it.  But it was my fault, and that's my punishment.  Not a fault of the design.

2.  Some combos and strategies do seem a little OP.  But they're not consistent enough to break the game.  And the game is fast enough that you it won't bother you much when it happens.  And if you're the one pulling it off, it feels pretty awesome.

Eric Lang's master opus.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2.5
Blood Rage relation to Citow is kinda like ... 
[i]you know that dude you knew at high school that was really into metal, wore long hair and did crazy stuff all the time? Now you meet him 15 years later and you barely recognize him in his business suit, short hair, immaculate attire. But he claims deep down he's still rock'n'roll and shows you a tiny tattoo on his ankle (under Hugo Boss sock). [/i]

Instead of figuring out how BR is a hybrid (if it is) it would easier to point out where it's not an euro.  
- There's drafting, but not 7W style, but more of MtG vibe as what you draft becomes your hand. 
- err ... that's it, the rest is quite euroey. 

Sure, there's combat. Which manages to be even more deterministic and calculable than in Smallworld. You count the value of your armies and compare numbers, add some more numbers hidden in your hand and voila. But the numbers from your hand aren't really hidden as they were firstly drafted and secondly if you lost a combat everybody knows what you have. So, no tension here. And tension is even more diluted because people don't necessarily care about winning as there are ways to get more points by losing a fight. Huh? It's a good sign a game is far far away from ameritrash when visceral enjoyment that makes playing the game fun does not giveth points. This game is like the Risk version with the least amount of risk(ing) possible. 

What bothered me the most is how designer controlled everything is and how little impact players as a collective have on the dynamics of the game. You're just doing what you're doing, countering other people's plans (not people directly!). Cards are orchestrated into three balanced eras (blah). Where's groupthink? Where's bashing on the leader? (okay, there might be some traces of this, but didn't see it in our game). 

Oh yeah, remember the area majority thing Citow had? It's kinda sorta still there, but diluted - some cards you draft allow you to score majorities. But: Firstly - getting majority is not as hard to accomplish (as you have a choice between 2-3 different areas). Secondly - quests are hidden. So, while traces of area majority remain, it creates no tension thus its soul is gone. 

Blood Rage seems like a study in how to take the structure of Citow and make it as euro-ey (balanced, calculable, tension-less) as possible. While the game isn't as optimisation prone and MPS-ey as workerplacements, you can pick old school euros like T&E or El Grande and they have more player dynamics, more tension, more psychology, more people in them! 

Maybe this game is actually a different type of dude than I described above. 
[i]It's the metal dude guy you meet, but turns out, that's just his visual attire as he's managing 10 bands, organising 3 festivals, while having another million dollar business on the side, a yacht, and a villa in the posh part of town, and of course he's married into a rich political family. The metal thing -   merely make up.[/i]
(Yeah, those minis... just bling on top of an euro)

RATING: 7.5
I love this game. Not necessarily one that gets to the table very often but it has beautiful production quality. I was lucky enough to run into Eric Lang at an unpub convention and got him to sign/doodle on my box cover for this game. I wish I had been into the hobby with this kickstarted but... all I can do is look forward to the future (a.k.a Rising Sun's KS campaign ha!).

This game features a variety of cool mechanisms that work quite nicely together. Card drafting was the thing that initially peaked my interest. The cards range from upgrades for your various engine components (military, ship, etc.), combat points and abilities, and secret objective cards that score you points for a variety of things (e.g. area control, dying in battle, etc.). Love this one!

RATING: 9
This is a very fun and interesting hybrid game. It combines drafting, action points, and combat mechanisms.

Over the course of the game every player will develop a unique clan that has it's own unique strengths and approach to earning glory. And each approach is a legitimate winning strategy, if executed well. Speaking of earning glory, the gameplay and the theme (of viking clans vieing to earn glory before ragnorok) are perfectly integrated.

Finally, it has to be said - this game is gorgeous, especially if you paint the figures. The Kickstarter extras are great, but I haven't felt deprived for not having them. Set up this game at a meetup and you will _always_ attract potential players.

A  fighting game that can be taught and learned very quickly, offers multiple paths to victory AND plays pretty quickly...this is the only one that I know in my collection that ticks off all those boxes.
